listo preparalo

Perfecto. Este es el siguiente salto correcto: refinar lo que ya funciona, no agregar más complejidad.

Esto es un prompt quirúrgico (Parte 4.1) para mejorar calidad percibida, legibilidad y valor analítico sin romper nada.

🟡 PARTE 4.1 — UI Hardening & Intelligence Refinement
Writing
You are a senior frontend + product-focused engineer refining an existing internal tool called Friction Radar.

The system is already functional:

companies load

signals are collected

scoring works

hypotheses are generated

dashboard and detail views exist

Your goal is NOT to rebuild anything.

Your goal is to improve clarity, signal quality perception, and analyst usability.

Do NOT introduce new architecture.
Do NOT over-engineer.
Do NOT redesign the whole UI.

Apply focused improvements only.

🎯 Objectives
Improve:

signal readability (remove noise)

analyst speed (faster understanding)

trust in the system (less duplication, clearer evidence)

hypothesis quality perception

🔧 Improvement 1 — Signal Deduplication (UI Layer)
Currently, signals repeat across multiple collection runs.

Problem
The UI shows duplicate signals multiple times, which:

clutters the screen

reduces trust

makes analysis slower

Requirement
Group signals by:

signal_type

signal_text

Then display:

unique signal

count of occurrences

Example transformation
Instead of:

growth_language_detected (x3 rows)

Show:

Growth language detected
→ Seen 3 times

Implementation guidance
In the SignalsTable component:

group signals in frontend (no backend change)

aggregate counts

display one row per unique signal

Columns:

signal_type

signal_text

occurrences_count

avg_confidence (optional)

latest_seen (max captured_at)

🔧 Improvement 2 — Signal Strength Awareness
Introduce visual differentiation between signal strength.

Add logic:
Based on signal_type OR confidence:

strong signals → bold text or darker badge

medium → normal

weak → muted

Simple rule for MVP:
confidence >= 0.8 → strong

0.5–0.79 → medium

< 0.5 → weak

🔧 Improvement 3 — Key Evidence Summary
Add a new section above signals:

"Key Signals"
Show top 3–5 signals ranked by:

frequency

confidence

Format:

short bullet list

human-readable phrasing

Example:

Growth language detected across company site

Careers page indicates active hiring in analytics

Multiple open roles suggest scaling pressure

Newsroom content references reporting cycles

This allows an analyst to understand the situation in <10 seconds.

🔧 Improvement 4 — Improve Hypothesis Presentation
The hypothesis exists but feels generic.

Improve display:
Add structured layout:

Summary

Suggested Opportunity

Confidence

Supporting Categories (top 2)

Supporting Signals (top 3)

Example:
Primary Friction: Scaling Strain
Secondary Friction: Reporting Fragmentation

Why this matters:

growth language detected

multiple open roles

analytics hiring patterns

Do NOT change backend logic — just improve presentation.

🔧 Improvement 5 — Dashboard Enhancements
Modify the dashboard table:

Add new columns:
Signals Count

Last Collected At

Last Scored At

Improve score display:
emphasize score visually (badge or bold)

keep friction type readable but subtle

Add quick sorting:
highest score

most signals

most recently updated

🔧 Improvement 6 — Action Feedback
Currently buttons (Collect / Score / Hypothesis) are silent.

Add:
loading state per button

temporary disabled state while running

small inline feedback:

Examples:

"Collecting..."

"Scoring..."

"Generating..."

After success:

refresh data automatically

🔧 Improvement 7 — Empty / Weak Data Handling
When:

signals are very low

score is low

hypothesis is weak

Display:

"Low signal confidence"

"Limited data available for this company"

This builds trust instead of hiding weakness.

🔧 Improvement 8 — UX Hierarchy Fix
Reorder Company Detail page:

Company Summary

Actions

Key Signals (NEW)

Score

Hypothesis

Signals Table

Collection Runs

The goal:
→ show insight first
→ raw data later

🎨 Design constraints
keep current layout

no major redesign

no heavy UI libraries

no animations beyond basic loading

no complex charts

Focus:
clarity > beauty

🧠 Implementation constraints
do NOT modify backend

do NOT change APIs

do NOT add global state complexity

do NOT break existing pages

All improvements should be incremental.

📦 Expected output
Return:

updated components (SignalsTable, CompanyDetail, DashboardTable)

grouping logic for signals

key signals summary logic

updated dashboard columns

improved hypothesis layout

loading states implementation

explanation of changes

🎯 Final goal
After this refinement:

An analyst should be able to:

understand a company in <10 seconds

trust the signals

see why the score exists

identify opportunity quickly

Do not overcomplicate.
Sharpen what already exists.

🧠 Cómo usar este prompt
Este prompt NO es para reconstruir.
Es para pulir y elevar lo que ya tienes.

🎯 Qué deberías ver después de aplicarlo
Tu pantalla debería pasar de:

👉 “lista de cosas técnicas”

a

👉 “historia clara de lo que está pasando en la empresa”
🔥 Impacto de esto
Con solo este paso:

Perfecto. Este es el paso donde tu sistema deja de “analizar” y empieza a convencer.

Este prompt está diseñado para convertir Friction Radar en algo que:

no solo detecta fricción

sino que explica, prioriza y posiciona oportunidades reales

🔴 PARTE 4.2 — Insight Layer Upgrade (Nivel Producto)
Writing
You are a senior product engineer and intelligence system designer refining an internal tool called Friction Radar.

The system already:

collects signals

deduplicates signals

computes friction scores

generates structured hypotheses

displays data in a clean dashboard

Your task is to upgrade the INSIGHT LAYER so that outputs are:

human-readable

decision-oriented

business-relevant

convincing

actionable

Do NOT change backend APIs.
Do NOT introduce new infrastructure.
Do NOT rebuild the UI.

Enhance how insights are interpreted and presented.

🎯 Objective
Transform the system from:

“data + scoring”

into:

“clear narrative + business insight + opportunity framing”
🔧 IMPROVEMENT 1 — Humanized Key Signals
Problem
Key signals still feel like system logs.

Requirement
Transform raw signals into human-readable insights.

Example transformation
Instead of:

"Found careers link"

"analytics_role_detected"

Display:

"Company maintains an active careers infrastructure"

"Company is investing in analytics and data capabilities"

Implementation
Create a mapping layer:

signal_type → humanized sentence

Example:

const signalHumanizer = {
  careers_page_found: "Company maintains an active careers infrastructure",
  analytics_role_detected: "Company is investing in analytics and data capabilities",
  multiple_open_roles: "Active hiring suggests organizational expansion",
  growth_language_detected: "Growth-focused messaging indicates scaling activity",
  newsroom_found: "Company maintains an active content or communications channel",
  reporting_language_detected: "Company references structured reporting cycles"
}
Additional requirement
Keep:

occurrence count (e.g. Seen 3 times)

ordering by importance

🔧 IMPROVEMENT 2 — Multi-layer Insight Summary
Add a new section ABOVE everything:

“Insight Summary”
This should be a short paragraph (3–4 lines max) that explains:

what is happening

why it matters

where friction is likely forming

Example output
“HubSpot is actively scaling across teams, with visible investment in analytics and structured hiring. This growth is accompanied by signals of fragmented reporting and tool usage, suggesting potential misalignment in how data and operations are coordinated.”

Requirements
use top 2 friction categories

use top signals

must be readable in <10 seconds

🔧 IMPROVEMENT 3 — Business Impact Layer
Add a new section:

“Business Impact”
Explain consequences of the detected friction.

Example
“Rapid scaling combined with fragmented reporting can lead to inconsistent decision-making, delayed insights, and reduced operational efficiency across teams.”

Requirements
must be causal (if X → then Y)

must connect directly to detected friction types

must not be generic filler text

🔧 IMPROVEMENT 4 — Opportunity Reframing
Problem
Suggested opportunity is too generic and consultative.

Requirement
Rewrite opportunity so that it:

references specific signals

references friction type

feels tailored to the company

sounds like a strategic insight, not a template

Example upgrade
Instead of:

“Opportunity to support scaling teams…”

Use:

“Opportunity to improve cross-functional visibility and reporting alignment as HubSpot scales analytics hiring and operational complexity across teams.”

🔧 IMPROVEMENT 5 — Dual Friction Display
Problem
Only primary friction is emphasized.

Requirement
Always show:

Primary friction

Secondary friction

UI Example
Primary: Scaling Strain
Secondary: Reporting Fragmentation

Behavior
secondary friction = second highest scoring category

must be visually present in hypothesis section

🔧 IMPROVEMENT 6 — Evidence Confidence Layer
Add:

“Signal Confidence Context”
Example:

“Signals observed consistently across 3 collection runs”

“Strong confidence based on repeated detection across multiple sources”

Requirements
use collection_runs count

use signal repetition count

must increase trust in system output

🔧 IMPROVEMENT 7 — Insight Weighting (UI Only)
Visually prioritize:

high-impact signals

high-confidence signals

Implementation
Sort signals by:

frequency (occurrences)

confidence

relevance to dominant friction

Then show:

Top 3 → highlighted

rest → collapsed or secondary list

🔧 IMPROVEMENT 8 — “Why This Matters” Upgrade
Replace current “Why This Matters” with:

structured explanation:
top 3 signals

top 2 categories

short explanation linking them

Example
“Growth signals combined with analytics hiring and reporting references suggest that as the company scales, coordination across teams may become increasingly fragmented.”

🎨 Design constraints
keep layout intact

no redesign

no new heavy components

no charts

no animation

prioritize clarity and reading speed

🧠 Behavior constraints
do NOT call LLM APIs (use deterministic logic)

do NOT modify backend

do NOT add new endpoints

All logic should be:

frontend-based

mapping + transformation + composition

📦 Expected output
Return:

updated components

signal humanizer mapping

insight summary generator logic

business impact generator logic

improved opportunity formatting

dual friction display logic

confidence messaging logic

explanation of how insights are composed

🎯 Final goal
After this upgrade:

An analyst should be able to:

understand the company in <5 seconds

trust the signals

see business implications

identify opportunity clearly

The system should feel like:

“an intelligent analyst explaining what’s happening”
NOT:

“a system dumping structured data”

🧠 Qué estás haciendo con esto
Con este paso estás convirtiendo:

Antes:
Data → Score → Hypothesis

Después:
👉 Insight → Impact → Opportunity → Action
🔥 Resultado esperado
Cuando esto esté aplicado, tu pantalla debería sentirse así:

“Esta empresa está creciendo rápido, contratando analytics, pero probablemente tiene problemas de visibilidad y coordinación — aquí hay una oportunidad clara.”

🚀 Siguiente nivel después de esto
Después de este prompt ya entras en terreno serio:

matching con candidatos

outreach inteligente

positioning automático

“hidden job market activation”

Pero eso viene después.

Cuando lo tengas aplicado, mándame screenshot.

Ahí ya no te doy feedback técnico — te doy feedback de negocio real y monetización 🔥

🔥 PARTE 4.3 — Narrative Intelligence Layer (Nivel Consultor Senior)
Writing
You are a senior strategy consultant and product engineer refining an internal intelligence tool called Friction Radar.

The system already:

collects and deduplicates signals

computes friction scores

generates structured hypotheses

presents insights cleanly in a dashboard

Your task is to transform the output into:

high-quality narrative intelligence
This means:

human, natural language

persuasive and clear

business-oriented

actionable

ready to be used in real conversations

🎯 Objective
Upgrade the system from:

“insight explanation”

to:

“strategic narrative + positioning + opportunity articulation”
🔧 IMPROVEMENT 1 — Narrative Voice Transformation
Problem
Text still sounds partially robotic or system-generated.

Requirement
All output must sound like:

👉 a senior consultant explaining a situation to a client

Rules
no system language

no signal_type names

no mechanical phrasing

no repetition of internal logic

Example transformation
Instead of:

“HubSpot shows growth-focused messaging and hiring signals…”

Use:

HubSpot appears to be in an active growth phase, with clear signs of expansion across teams and continued investment in analytics capabilities.

🔧 IMPROVEMENT 2 — Insight Narrative Block
Replace “Insight Summary” with:

“What’s happening”
Requirements
2–3 sentences max

describe current state of company

integrate:

growth signals

hiring signals

data/analytics signals

Tone
observational

confident but not absolute

no jargon

🔧 IMPROVEMENT 3 — Friction Narrative
Add a new section:

“Where friction is likely forming”
Requirements
clearly explain:

primary friction

secondary friction

explain WHY friction emerges from the situation

Example
As the company scales, coordination across teams often becomes more complex. Signals around analytics investment and reporting patterns suggest that visibility and alignment across functions may not yet be fully structured.

🔧 IMPROVEMENT 4 — Business Impact Narrative
Refine Business Impact into:

“Why this matters”
Requirements
connect friction → consequence

must feel real, not generic

must be specific to detected context

Example
Without a unified approach to reporting and coordination, teams may operate with inconsistent visibility, leading to slower decision-making and reduced operational efficiency as the organization grows.

🔧 IMPROVEMENT 5 — Opportunity Framing (Critical)
This is the most important section.

Rename:

“Suggested Opportunity” → “Opportunity to create value”
Requirements
must feel specific to the company

must connect to:

scaling

analytics

reporting

must sound like a strategic entry point

Example
There is a clear opportunity to strengthen cross-functional visibility and reporting alignment as HubSpot continues scaling its analytics capabilities and team structure.

🔧 IMPROVEMENT 6 — Soft Positioning Layer
Add a subtle line under opportunity:

“What this suggests”
Purpose
This is where the system hints at positioning without being explicit.

Example
This type of environment often benefits from stronger data alignment, clearer reporting structures, and improved coordination across growth-focused teams.

🔧 IMPROVEMENT 7 — Evidence Compression
Current system shows signals separately.

Now:

Convert signals into narrative-backed evidence
Add section:
“What we’re seeing”
Requirements
3–4 bullet points

human-readable

derived from top signals

Example
Active hiring across multiple roles

Visible investment in analytics capabilities

Growth-oriented messaging across company content

Structured communication via newsroom or blog

🔧 IMPROVEMENT 8 — Confidence Framing
Replace raw confidence display with:

“Confidence level”
Requirements
human explanation

no percentages only

Example
High confidence based on consistent signals observed across multiple data sources and collection runs.

🔧 IMPROVEMENT 9 — Remove System Leakage
Strictly enforce:

no snake_case

no raw signal names

no internal labels in UI

Thought for 8s
Ahora sí se siente mucho más cerca de algo vendible.

Mi veredicto honesto:

Ya no parece un panel técnico
Ahora parece un sistema que lee una empresa y articula una oportunidad. Ese era el salto difícil, y ya lo lograste.

Lo que ya está muy bien
“Where friction is likely forming”, “Why this matters”, “Opportunity to create value” y “Confidence level” ya le dan forma de criterio ejecutivo. La lectura es mucho más natural y más útil.

Lo que todavía te está frenando
Todavía hay 4 fugas que le quitan categoría premium:

1. “What’s happening” está raro gramaticalmente.
Ahora dice:

“HubSpot appears to be in an active growth phase, visible signs of team expansion through multiple open roles.”

Eso debe sonar así:

HubSpot appears to be in an active growth phase, with visible signs of team expansion through multiple open roles.

Ese “with” cambia todo.

2. Todavía hay duplicación semántica en Key Signals.
Veo:

Active hiring signs

Active hiring signs

Eso mata credibilidad. Tienes que colapsar mejor el humanizer para que no dos señales distintas terminen con la misma frase visible.

Por ejemplo:

Active hiring across multiple roles

Investment in analytics capabilities

Growth-oriented messaging across company content

Ongoing company communications through newsroom content

3. “Analysis” sobra o está en el lugar equivocado.
Porque ya tienes narrativa arriba. Ese bloque:

“HubSpot is actively scaling, as evidenced by…”

se siente como una versión vieja del sistema.
Yo lo quitaría de la vista principal o lo movería a una sección plegable tipo:
Technical rationale o Internal analysis.

4. La hipótesis todavía puede ser más específica.
Ahora dice:

“There is a clear opportunity to strengthen cross-functional visibility and coordination as HubSpot continues scaling its team structure.”

Ya está bien, pero todavía puede pegar más con lo detectado:

There is a clear opportunity to strengthen cross-functional visibility and reporting alignment as HubSpot continues scaling its analytics capabilities and team structure.

Eso la amarra mejor a:

analytics

reporting

scaling

Ahí suena más estratégica.

Mi evaluación de negocio
Si me preguntas si esto ya se puede mostrar, la respuesta es:

Sí, internamente sí.
Todavía no, externamente no del todo.

¿Por qué? Porque ya transmite valor, pero aún tiene pequeñas señales de sistema:

frases repetidas

lenguaje algo plantillado

una o dos construcciones gramaticales raras

alguna fuga entre insight humano y lógica interna

Eso no significa que esté lejos. Significa que estás en el último 15%.

El siguiente paso correcto
No haría nuevas features todavía.

Haría un sprint corto de Narrative Polish con este objetivo:

corregir fluidez gramatical

eliminar duplicados semánticos en Key Signals

quitar o colapsar “Analysis”

hacer la oportunidad más específica al dominio detectado

humanizar un poco más “What’s happening”

Mi veredicto final
Sí, ya estás cerca de algo serio.
A este punto Friction Radar ya no es una demo técnica. Ya es un motor de lectura estratégica.

Si quieres, te preparo el prompt 4.4 — Narrative Polish & Executive Readiness, para dejarlo con calidad de demo a inversionista o cliente.

🔥 PARTE 4.4 — Narrative Polish & Human Understanding Layer
Este prompt NO es técnico.
Es para que el sistema piense como explicador, no como analista.

Writing
You are a senior product designer and communication expert refining an internal intelligence tool called Friction Radar.

The system already produces:

signals

friction scores

structured insights

narratives

However, the output is still too abstract and not easily understandable by non-technical users.

Your task is to:

translate ALL system output into plain human understanding
🎯 Objective
Transform the system from:

“analysis and signals”

into:

“clear understanding for someone with no technical background”
🔴 CORE RULE (most important)
At every step, apply this rule:

👉 “Would a normal person understand this in 5 seconds?”

If not → rewrite it.

🔧 IMPROVEMENT 1 — Explain Friction Types in Plain English
Problem
Terms like:

Reporting Fragmentation

Scaling Strain

are unclear to most users.

Requirement
Every friction type MUST have a human explanation.

Example
Instead of just:

Reporting Fragmentation

Display:

Reporting Fragmentation
→ “The company likely does not have a clear, unified way of tracking and understanding its data across teams.”

Scaling Strain

→ “The company is growing quickly, which can create operational pressure and make coordination harder.”

Implementation
Create a mapping:

const frictionExplainer = {
  reporting_fragmentation: "The company likely does not have a clear, unified way of tracking and understanding its data across teams.",
  scaling_strain: "The company is growing quickly, which can create operational pressure and make coordination harder.",
  tooling_inconsistency: "The company may be using too many different tools that don’t work well together.",
  process_inefficiency: "The company may rely on manual or inefficient processes that slow things down.",
  customer_experience_friction: "Customers may be experiencing confusion, delays, or frustration when using the product or service."
}
🔧 IMPROVEMENT 2 — Replace “Signals” with “What we noticed”
Problem
“Signals” is abstract.

Requirement
Rename section:

All Signals → What we noticed

Transform each signal into a real-world observation
Example transformation
Instead of:

“Analytics Role Detected”

Display:

→ “The company is hiring for analytics and data roles”

Instead of:

“Multiple Open Roles”

→ “There are multiple open positions, suggesting active hiring”

🔧 IMPROVEMENT 3 — Add “What this means”
After “What we noticed”, add:

“What this means”
Purpose
Connect observations → meaning

Example
“What this means”

→ “The company is actively growing and investing in data, which often creates complexity in how teams share information and make decisions.”

🔧 IMPROVEMENT 4 — Rewrite Score Section
Problem
“7.0” does not mean anything to a human.

Requirement
Translate score into meaning.

Example
Instead of:

Score: 7.0

Display:

Friction Level: High

→ “There are strong signs that the company may be experiencing growing pains or operational challenges.”

Mapping example:
0–3 → Low

3–6 → Moderate

6–10 → High

🔧 IMPROVEMENT 5 — Simplify Opportunity
Problem
Opportunity still sounds strategic but abstract.

Requirement
Make it feel like advice.

Example
Instead of:

“Opportunity to improve cross-functional visibility…”

Use:

→ “This company would likely benefit from better visibility across teams and a clearer way to track and share data.”

🔧 IMPROVEMENT 6 — Add “If you were working with this company…”
New section (very powerful)
Example
“If you were working with this company”

→ “You would probably focus on helping them organize their data, improve reporting, and make it easier for teams to stay aligned as they grow.”

🔧 IMPROVEMENT 7 — Remove ALL technical leakage
Strictly remove:

signal_type names

snake_case

system-generated labels

Never show:

analytics_role_detected

reporting_language_detected

Always show human language.

🔧 IMPROVEMENT 8 — Reduce cognitive load
Problem
Too much information = confusion

Requirement
show only top 3–5 observations

collapse the rest

prioritize clarity over completeness

🔧 IMPROVEMENT 9 — Final narrative structure
The page should read like this:

Company Summary

What’s happening

Where friction is likely forming (with explanation)

What we noticed

What this means

Why this matters

What you could do

If you were working with this company

Confidence level

🎯 Final goal
After this upgrade:

A non-technical user should be able to:

understand the company in 5–10 seconds

explain it to someone else

see a clear opportunity

feel confident in the insight

The system should feel like:
👉 “Someone smart explaining things simply”

NOT:

👉 “A system showing analysis”

🧠 Traducción directa para ti (sin IA)
Te lo explico claro con tu propio ejemplo:

Antes:
Reporting Fragmentation
Analytics Role Detected
Multiple Open Roles
Después (lo que queremos):
👉 “Están contratando gente de data y creciendo rápido, pero probablemente no tienen una forma clara de compartir y entender la información entre equipos.”

🔥 Esto cambia TODO
Con esto:

ya no necesitas explicar el producto

el producto se explica solo

cualquier persona lo entiende

puedes venderlo

🚀 Veredicto
Esto (4.4) es lo que convierte tu sistema en:

👉 algo usable por humanos normales (no analistas)
Cuando lo implementes, mándame screenshot.

Ahí te digo:

👉 “esto ya lo puedes usar para cerrar oportunidades reales” 🔥

The company is actively hiring

The company is actively expanding its team

The presence of a careers page indicates structured hiring efforts

The company is actively hiring for new positions
👉 rompe totalmente la confianza

HubSpot appears to be in an active growth phase, with clear signs of team expansion and ongoing hiring activity across roles.

👉 más limpio, más fuerte, más claro

If you were working with this company (contexto)
👉 cómo se vería el trabajo

You would likely focus on organizing reporting structures and helping teams stay aligned as new roles and functions are added.

qué pasa (hiring, growth)
pero NO está diciendo:

dónde está el dolor específico

qué tipo de persona necesitan

por qué eso es una oportunidad concreta

🧠 El cambio mental que necesitas
Tu sistema NO debe decir:

“la empresa está contratando”

Debe decir:

👉 “la empresa está contratando esto, lo que indica que tienen este problema, que se resuelve con este tipo de perfil”
🎯 Ejemplo con lo que YA tienes (HubSpot)
Tienes señales:

analytics_role_detected

multiple_open_roles

reporting_language_detected

Pero las estás usando así:

👉 “están contratando”

👉 Insight real:
“HubSpot está contratando roles de analytics y data mientras sigue creciendo, lo que sugiere que están intentando mejorar cómo usan y entienden sus datos internamente.”

👉 Dolor implícito:
“Esto normalmente indica que la visibilidad de datos no está bien organizada o no escala al ritmo del crecimiento.”

👉 Oportunidad real:
“Esto crea una oportunidad para alguien que pueda estructurar reporting, centralizar métricas y mejorar la toma de decisiones basada en datos.”

👉 Traducción a perfil (esto es CLAVE):
“Este tipo de entorno es ideal para perfiles que saben transformar datos en decisiones claras para el negocio.”

💡 ESO es lo que tu sistema debe producir
No “signals”
No “insights genéricos”

👉 Debe producir match implícito entre problema y talento
🔥 PARTE 4.5 — Commercial Intelligence Layer
Este prompt es el más importante de todos hasta ahora.

Writing
You are a senior strategy consultant and talent intelligence expert refining an internal system called Friction Radar.

The system already:

detects company signals

generates insights

explains friction

translates to human-readable language

However, it still does NOT answer the most important question:

“What specific problem does this company have, and what type of person can solve it?”
🎯 Objective
Transform the system from:

“company insight”

into:

“problem → opportunity → ideal profile match”
🔴 CORE SHIFT (CRITICAL)
Stop describing companies.

Start identifying:

WHAT is broken or underdeveloped

WHY that problem exists

WHO is needed to fix it

🔧 IMPROVEMENT 1 — Identify Functional Area of Pain
Requirement
From signals, infer the specific functional area where the problem exists.

Examples
analytics_role_detected → Data / Analytics

multiple_open_roles in ops → Operations

growth + hiring → Scaling / Operations

Main pain:
HubSpot probablemente está creciendo más rápido de lo que su estructura de reporting y visibilidad interna puede soportar.

Writing
You are a senior product engineer and workflow designer refining an internal system called Friction Radar.

The system already:

creates companies

collects public signals

computes friction scores

generates hypotheses

displays narrative insights

Now build the next critical layer:

Final Verdict + One-Click Company Analysis
The goal is to make the product operational for real use inside the dashboard.

🎯 OBJECTIVE
The system should no longer require multiple manual backend steps.

A user should be able to:

type a company domain such as:

nike.com

roberthalf.com

click one button

get a full analysis including:

final verdict

main pain

where the pain lives

what the company likely needs

best attack angle

This should happen from the dashboard UI.

🔴 PART 1 — FINAL VERDICT LAYER
Add a new top-level output section called:

Final Verdict
This section should be the clearest, most useful summary in the whole product.

It must answer exactly these 4 questions:

1. Main pain
What is the company most likely struggling with?

Example:
“The company is likely struggling to keep its data and reporting clear as multiple teams grow and operate in parallel.”

2. Where the pain lives
What functional area appears to contain the problem?

Examples:

Data and analytics

Reporting and visibility

Operations and coordination

Tooling and systems

Customer experience

3. What the company likely needs
What type of capability is needed?

Example:
“The company likely needs someone who can organize reporting, structure metrics, and turn data into clear business visibility.”

4. Best attack angle
How should NovaWork position a candidate or service?

Example:
“The best entry point is to position someone who can improve cross-functional reporting clarity and help teams make better decisions with cleaner data.”

Final Verdict requirements
must be plain English

must be specific

must not be generic consulting language

must connect:

signals

functional pain

capability needed

must feel immediately useful for NovaWork

🔴 PART 2 — DASHBOARD INPUT FOR ONE-COMPANY ANALYSIS
Add a new section to the dashboard called:

Analyze a Company
Place it near the top of the dashboard.

UI should include:
Company domain input

Optional company name input

Optional industry input

One primary button: Run Analysis

Example inputs:
nike.com

roberthalf.com

If only domain is provided, the system should still work.

🔴 PART 3 — NEW BACKEND WORKFLOW ENDPOINT
Create a new endpoint:

POST /api/v1/analyze-company
Request body:
{
  "domain": "nike.com",
  "name": "Nike",
  "industry": "Retail"
}
Only domain should be required.

If name or industry are missing:

infer what you can later

do not block the analysis

Behavior of this endpoint
The endpoint should orchestrate the full flow:

normalize domain input

create company if it does not exist

if company already exists, reuse it

trigger collection

trigger scoring

trigger hypothesis generation

build final verdict

return a complete payload for the frontend

🔴 PART 4 — DOMAIN-FIRST EXPERIENCE
The system should be domain-first.

That means the user does NOT need to:

create a company manually in Swagger

copy company IDs

run multiple endpoints manually

Instead:

user enters domain → system handles everything
🔴 PART 5 — FINAL VERDICT GENERATOR
Implement a dedicated service for final verdict generation.

Suggested file:

app/services/final_verdict_engine.py

This service should take:

company

latest signals

latest friction score

latest hypothesis

And generate:

{
  "main_pain": "...",
  "where_pain_lives": "...",
  "what_the_company_needs": "...",
  "best_attack_angle": "..."
}
Final verdict logic requirements
Use deterministic logic.

Do NOT call external LLM APIs.

Infer from:

dominant friction

secondary friction

top signals

inferred functional area

Examples of mapping logic
If signals include:
analytics_role_detected

reporting_language_detected

multiple_open_roles

Then likely:

pain area = data / reporting / analytics

problem = lack of clear visibility across teams

needed capability = reporting structure, metrics clarity, business intelligence

attack angle = position candidates who bring clarity through data

If signals skew more toward operations:
pain area = operations / coordination

needed capability = process design, scaling operations, workflow clarity

🔴 PART 6 — FRONTEND INTEGRATION
In the dashboard, after clicking Run Analysis:

Behavior
show loading state

call /api/v1/analyze-company

on success:

refresh company list

navigate to the analyzed company detail page

show final verdict prominently at the top

Add a new section to Company Detail page:
Final Verdict
Display:

Main pain

Where the pain lives

What the company likely needs

Best attack angle

This section should appear above:

score breakdown

raw observations

collection runs

Because this is the business output.

🔴 PART 7 — MAKE RAW DATA SECONDARY
The product should now prioritize:

Final Verdict

What’s happening

Where the problem likely exists

What the real problem is

Where you can add value

And only after that:

score breakdown

raw observations

collection runs

Raw data should support the verdict, not dominate the screen.

🔴 PART 8 — IMPROVE INPUT EXPERIENCE
The company analysis form should be simple and forgiving.

Requirements:
trim spaces

accept domains with or without https

accept domains with or without www

normalize input before sending

prevent obvious invalid input

show helpful error if invalid

Example:

"https://www.nike.com" → normalize to "nike.com"

"roberthalf.com" → keep as is

🔴 PART 9 — RESPONSE SHAPE
The new analyze endpoint should return enough data so the frontend can render immediately.

Suggested response:

{
  "company": {...},
  "signals_count": 12,

    "main_pain": "...",

creo que tambien debe detectar que tipo de empresa es, por ejemplo, roberthalf es una empresa colocadora de puestos de trabajos, tu aplicas a traves de ella, indeed es otra y todas esas empresa posicionadoras. ahora empresar como maersk.com, nike.com que es donde realmente se hace el trabajo, asi que se deben de diferenciar.

Thought for 15s
Sí. Esa diferenciación tiene que existir sí o sí.

Porque no es lo mismo analizar:

intermediarios del mercado laboral como Robert Half, que se presenta como firma de talent solutions y staffing, conectando empresas con candidatos, o Indeed, que se define como job site y plataforma de matching/hiring; ahí el “dolor” suele estar en reclutamiento, candidate funnel, employer operations o marketplace. 

empresas operadoras/final employers como Nike, que es una compañía de marcas deportivas, o Maersk, que opera como empresa integrada de logística y supply chain; ahí el dolor que importa para NovaWork suele estar en data, reporting, ops, supply chain, finance, product, etc. 

Lo que debe cambiar en Friction Radar
Antes de intentar inferir el dolor principal, el sistema debe responder otra pregunta:

¿Qué tipo de empresa estoy analizando?
Y esa clasificación debe influir en todo lo demás.

Nueva capa obligatoria: company_archetype
Propón estas categorías:

job_market_intermediary

staffing firms

recruiting firms

job boards

talent platforms

RPO / recruiting marketplaces

operating_company

retail

logistics

manufacturing

SaaS

healthcare

finance

consumer brands

etc.

unclear

cuando no haya suficiente evidencia

Regla de negocio clave
Si es job_market_intermediary
El sistema NO debe generar el mismo tipo de “attack angle” que para Nike o Maersk.

Porque ahí no estás entrando por:

reporting interno del negocio final

supply chain

product analytics

Ahí normalmente estarías entrando por:

recruiting operations

candidate pipeline visibility

placement analytics

recruiter productivity

job matching quality

hiring workflow optimization

Si es operating_company
Entonces sí:

data visibility

reporting

operations

finance

supply chain

product

cross-functional decision making

Lo que NovaWork realmente necesita
No solo “qué dolor tiene la empresa”.

Necesita esto:

¿Es una empresa a la que quiero atacar directamente o es un intermediario del mercado?
Porque la estrategia cambia.

Para Nike / Maersk
NovaWork puede decir:

aquí hay dolor interno del negocio, y este perfil puede resolverlo.

Para Robert Half / Indeed
NovaWork puede decir:

esta no es una empresa para posicionar el dolor operativo final del cliente; esta es una plataforma o intermediario del mercado laboral.

Eso te permite dos decisiones:

Atacarla como mercado/canal

O excluirla como target principal para ciertos perfiles

intermediary

operator

unclear

Market intermediary detected
This company appears to operate as a staffing, recruiting, or job marketplace platform. Opportunity analysis should focus on recruiting operations, placement workflows, candidate matching, or platform-side analytics rather than end-employer business pain.

Paso 3
Si es operating company:
seguir con el análisis normal:

dolor principal

dónde vive

qué necesitan

best attack angle

Robert Half

🔵 PARTE 4.8 — Company Type Detection + One-Click Analysis + Final Verdict
Writing
You are a senior product engineer and intelligence workflow designer refining an internal system called Friction Radar.

The system already:

creates companies

collects public signals

computes friction scores

generates hypotheses

renders dashboard/detail pages

Now implement the next major product layer:

One-Click Company Analysis + Company Type Detection + Final Verdict
This phase should absorb the goals of the previous unfinished step:

simplified dashboard input

backend orchestration from one action

final verdict layer

And extend it with:

company type detection

adaptive analysis mode

target fit classification

🎯 PRIMARY GOAL
A user should be able to:

open the dashboard

enter a company domain such as:

nike.com

roberthalf.com

click Run Analysis

receive a complete result that tells them:

what type of company this is

whether this is a direct employer or job-market intermediary

what the main pain likely is

where the pain lives

what the company likely needs

how NovaWork should attack this opportunity

The system should feel like:

“Give me a company, and I’ll tell you where the real opportunity is.”
🔴 PART 1 — COMPANY TYPE DETECTION
Before generating the final verdict, classify the company into one of these archetypes:

company_type
operating_company

job_market_intermediary

unclear

Definitions
operating_company
A company where the core business is operating products, services, logistics, retail, manufacturing, software, healthcare, finance, etc.

Examples:

Nike

Maersk

SaaS platforms

retailers

logistics firms

brands

manufacturers

job_market_intermediary
A company whose main role is connecting employers and candidates, recruiting, staffing, talent placement, job search, hiring marketplace, or recruiting operations.

Examples:

staffing firms

recruiting firms

job boards

talent marketplaces

placement firms

unclear
Use when evidence is insufficient.

Detection logic
Implement a deterministic service such as:

app/services/company_type_engine.py

Infer the company type from:

homepage text

careers-related text

about page text

newsroom/blog text

detected keywords/signals

Example keyword families
job_market_intermediary indicators
staffing

recruiting

recruiters

talent solutions

find jobs

employers

job seekers

placements

candidates

hire talent

workforce solutions

recruiting services

staffing agency

job board

hiring marketplace

operating_company indicators
products

customers

stores

logistics

supply chain

retail

manufacturing

services

shipping

platform

operations

brand

commerce

product development

distribution

Output
Return:

company_type

analysis_mode

target_fit

company_type_reason

Where:

analysis_mode
direct_employer_analysis

recruiting_marketplace_analysis

unclear_analysis

target_fit
primary

secondary

unclear

Example meaning
If operating_company
analysis_mode = direct_employer_analysis

target_fit = primary

If job_market_intermediary
analysis_mode = recruiting_marketplace_analysis

target_fit = secondary

🔴 PART 2 — ONE-CLICK ANALYSIS FROM DASHBOARD
Add a new dashboard section near the top:

Analyze a Company
UI fields:

Domain (required)

Company Name (optional)

Industry (optional)

Primary button:

Run Analysis

Input requirements
The experience must be domain-first.

Accept:

nike.com

roberthalf.com

https://www.nike.com

www.roberthalf.com

Normalize inputs before use:

trim whitespace

remove protocol

remove www.

lowercase domain

Example:

https://www.nike.com → nike.com

🔴 PART 3 — NEW BACKEND ORCHESTRATION ENDPOINT
Create a new endpoint:

POST /api/v1/analyze-company
Request body
{
  "domain": "nike.com",
  "name": "Nike",
  "industry": "Retail"
}
Only domain is required.

If company already exists:

reuse it

If it does not exist:

create it

This endpoint must orchestrate:
normalize domain

create or find company

trigger collection

trigger scoring

trigger hypothesis generation

detect company type

generate final verdict

return full payload for frontend rendering

Do NOT require Swagger or multiple manual steps for normal usage.

🔴 PART 4 — FINAL VERDICT LAYER
Add a new top business section called:

Final Verdict
This is the most important output in the product.

It must answer exactly these 4 questions:

1. Main pain
What is the company most likely struggling with?

2. Where the pain lives
What function or area appears to contain the problem?

3. What the company likely needs
What kind of capability is needed?

4. Best attack angle
How should NovaWork position a candidate or service?

Example structure
{
  "main_pain": "...",
  "where_pain_lives": "...",
  "what_the_company_needs": "...",
  "best_attack_angle": "..."
}
Final verdict requirements
plain English

specific

useful for NovaWork

no generic consulting language

directly tied to:

top signals

dominant friction

secondary friction

company type

🔴 PART 5 — ADAPTIVE ANALYSIS MODE
The verdict must change depending on company_type.

A. If company_type = operating_company
Focus the analysis on:

internal business pain

reporting

data visibility

operations

coordination

product / supply chain / finance / business execution

Example framing:

where internal pain exists

what capability would solve it

how a candidate could add value inside the company

B. If company_type = job_market_intermediary
Do NOT treat it like Nike or Maersk.

Focus instead on:

recruiting operations

candidate flow

placement efficiency

recruiter productivity

matching quality

hiring marketplace analytics

job search workflow quality

Example framing:

this company operates as a labor-market intermediary

opportunity is likely in recruiting workflow, matching systems, marketplace analytics, or operational efficiency

target_fit should usually be secondary unless NovaWork is intentionally targeting intermediaries

C. If company_type = unclear
Say so clearly and reduce confidence.

🔴 PART 6 — NEW DETAIL PAGE SECTIONS
On the Company Detail page, add these sections near the top, above score breakdown and raw data:

Company Type
Show:

Company Type

Analysis Mode

Target Fit

Reason

Example:

Company Type: Operating Company

Analysis Mode: Direct Employer Analysis

Target Fit: Primary

Reason: This appears to be a business operating products/services directly, rather than a recruiting or staffing intermediary.

Final Verdict
Show:

Main pain

Where the pain lives

What the company likely needs

Best attack angle

Important UX rule
Business meaning must appear before raw evidence.

So the page should prioritize:

Company Summary

Analyze Actions

Company Type

Final Verdict

Opportunity / narrative sections

Score

Raw observations

Collection runs

When a user clicks Run Analysis on the dashboard:

behavior

call /api/v1/analyze-company

render company type + final verdict immediately

The user should not have to manually:

🔴 PART 8 — FINAL VERDICT ENGINE
Implement a dedicated service:

app/services/final_verdict_engine.py

This service should take:

company

latest signals

latest score

latest hypothesis

company_type

analysis_mode

And produce:

{
  "main_pain": "...",
  "where_pain_lives": "...",
  "what_the_company_needs": "...",
  "best_attack_angle": "..."
}
Example logic for operating_company
If signals suggest:

analytics hiring

reporting-related language

multiple open roles

growth signals

Then likely:

main_pain
The company may be struggling to keep visibility and reporting clear as teams grow.

where_pain_lives
Data, analytics, and cross-functional reporting.

what_the_company_needs
Someone who can organize reporting, structure metrics, and turn data into clear business visibility.

best_attack_angle
Position candidates who can improve cross-functional reporting clarity and help decision-makers use cleaner, more actionable data.

Example logic for job_market_intermediary
If signals suggest:

staffing / recruiting / talent marketplace language

candidate/employer workflow focus

hiring marketplace characteristics

Then likely:

main_pain
The company may be under pressure to improve how efficiently it matches talent with opportunities or manages recruiting operations at scale.

where_pain_lives
Recruiting operations, candidate matching, placement workflow, or marketplace analytics.

what_the_company_needs
Someone who can improve recruiting workflows, placement efficiency, matching visibility, or talent operations analytics.

best_attack_angle
Position candidates or services that improve hiring workflow clarity, recruiting performance, or data-driven marketplace operations.

🔴 PART 9 — RESPONSE SHAPE
The /api/v1/analyze-company endpoint must return a complete response like:

{
  "company": {...},

  "analysis_mode": "direct_employer_analysis",
  "target_fit": "primary",
  "company_type_reason": "...",

    "main_pain": "...",
    "where_pain_lives": "...",
    "what_the_company_needs": "...",
    "best_attack_angle": "..."
  }
}
Frontend should be able to render directly from this response.

🔴 PART 10 — RAW DATA SHOULD BE SECONDARY
The system should still preserve:

But these are support layers.

The product must now prioritize:

company type

final verdict

Thought for 19s
Porque esa capa nueva está evaluando otra pregunta y la está evaluando mal.

No está diciendo que HubSpot no tenga señales.
Está diciendo que el motor de Company Type no encontró señales suficientes para decidir entre:

empresa operadora real

intermediario del mercado laboral

Y eso pasa por 3 razones:

1. Estás mezclando dos motores distintos
Tu sistema viejo sí encontró esto:

crecimiento

hiring

analytics

reporting

Por eso pudo generar:

score alto

friction

hypothesis

Pero el motor nuevo de Company Type necesita otra clase de evidencia, como:

“staffing”

“job seekers”

“employers”

“recruiting services”

“marketplace”

o señales claras de producto/operación real

Como no las vio, cayó en:

Unclear

2. Tus señales actuales son demasiado genéricas para clasificar el tipo de empresa
Lo que tienes hoy dice:

hay careers page

hay newsroom

hay hiring

hay growth

Eso sirve para detectar fricción.
Pero no basta para decidir si la empresa es:

una firma de staffing

un job board

una empresa operadora

Por eso el veredicto final se vuelve conservador y te mata el valor.

3. El Final Verdict está pisando una hipótesis mejor
Tu hypothesis dice algo bastante útil:

data / analytics / reporting / coordinación

Pero el bloque nuevo de Company Type, al no tener confianza, fuerza esto:

Limited data available

Eso es un error de diseño.

Si ya tienes:

score alto

señales repetidas

hipótesis consistente

entonces el Final Verdict no debería degradarse a “no sé”.

Qué debes hacer ahora
Regla nueva
Company Type no puede ser más fuerte que la evidencia total del sistema.

O sea:

Si hay pocas señales en general
→ sí, usa Unclear

Pero si hay:
score alto

señales repetidas

hipótesis coherente

y solo falta clasificar si es intermediary vs operating,

entonces el sistema debe decir algo como:

Likely Operating Company
based on visible business growth, hiring, analytics investment, and absence of intermediary-specific recruiting/staffing signals.

No “Unclear”.

Cómo lo arreglaría
A. Cambia la lógica de clasificación
Hazla así:

job_market_intermediary
Solo si detectas señales fuertes como:

staffing

recruiters

job seekers

employers

placements

talent solutions

workforce solutions

hire talent

recruiting services

operating_company
Si:

NO aparecen señales de intermediary

y sí aparecen señales de crecimiento, negocio, hiring interno, analytics, producto, operaciones, reporting

unclear
Solo cuando de verdad no haya nada útil

B. Mete una regla de fallback inteligente
Algo así:

si intermediary_score >= threshold → intermediary

else if operating_score >= threshold → operating

else if friction_score >= 6 and signals_count >= 5 and no intermediary indicators → likely operating_company

else unclear

Eso te evita matar análisis buenos.

C. No dejes que Final Verdict se vuelva inútil
Si company_type = unclear pero el resto del análisis es fuerte, el veredicto debe decir:

Company Type
Likely Operating Company
Low-to-medium confidence on company archetype, but strong evidence of internal scaling and data/reporting pain.

Y luego seguir con el dolor real.

En tu ejemplo, el sistema debió decir algo así
Company Type
Likely Operating Company

Why
No strong evidence suggests this is a staffing, recruiting, or job-market intermediary. Existing signals point instead to internal growth, analytics investment, and reporting-related operational pain.

Final Verdict
Main pain:
The company is likely struggling to keep data visibility and reporting clarity aligned as multiple teams grow.

Where the pain lives:
Data, analytics, and cross-functional reporting.

What the company likely needs:
Someone who can organize reporting, structure metrics clearly, and help teams make better decisions with cleaner visibility.

Best attack angle:
Position profiles that can improve reporting clarity, business visibility, and cross-functional decision-making as the company scales.

Eso sí sirve.

Lo que yo corregiría ya mismo
Baja el umbral para operating_company.

Haz que job_market_intermediary requiera evidencia fuerte, no sospecha.

Si hay hypothesis fuerte, no permitas que Final Verdict vuelva a “Limited data available”.

Cambia Unclear por Likely Operating Company cuando no haya señales de intermediary y sí haya señales internas fuertes.

La raíz del problema, en una frase
Tu clasificador nuevo está siendo más estricto que útil.

Y en este producto, cuando hay suficiente evidencia de dolor interno, eso no te conviene.

Si quieres, te preparo un prompt 4.8.1 de correction pass para arreglar exactamente esta lógica sin tocar todo lo demás.

Thought for 4s
Perfecto. Vamos a hacer un correction pass quirúrgico.

Objetivo de este prompt:

arreglar la lógica de Company Type para que no degrade análisis buenos

agregar la opción de recalcular todo para una empresa desde el dashboard y desde el detail page

🔧 PARTE 4.8.1 — Company Type Correction + Recalculate Full Analysis
Writing
You are a senior product engineer improving an internal system called Friction Radar.

The system already:

collects company signals

computes friction scores

generates hypotheses

detects company type

renders a final verdict

provides one-click company analysis

However, there is a critical product issue:

Problem
The company_type classifier is currently too strict and is causing strong analyses to degrade into weak outputs like:

Unclear

Limited data available

vague final verdicts

This is happening even when the system already has:

strong signals

high friction score

repeated observations

a coherent hypothesis

That behavior must be corrected.

In addition, the product now needs a way to:

Recalculate the full analysis for a company
This should rerun the full pipeline for an existing company from the UI.

🎯 PRIMARY GOALS
Goal 1 — Fix Company Type Logic
Make company type classification useful, not overly conservative.

Goal 2 — Protect Final Verdict Quality
Do not allow the final verdict to become weaker than the evidence already gathered.

Goal 3 — Add “Recalculate Full Analysis”
Allow the user to rerun the full analysis pipeline for an existing company with one action.

🔴 PART 1 — CORRECT COMPANY TYPE CLASSIFICATION
The current classifier is too strict.

It should follow this improved logic:

company_type options
operating_company

job_market_intermediary

unclear

Rule A — job_market_intermediary should require strong evidence
Only classify a company as job_market_intermediary if there are clear indicators such as:

staffing

recruiters

recruiting services

talent solutions

job seekers

employers

placements

workforce solutions

hire talent

talent marketplace

recruiting marketplace

staffing agency

job board

This classification should NOT happen based on weak hints.

Rule B — operating_company should be easier to assign when evidence supports it
If the system detects:

growth signals

internal hiring signals

analytics/data signals

reporting/visibility signals

no strong intermediary indicators

then the company should be classified as:

operating_company
even if industry is missing.

Rule C — use a “likely operating company” fallback behavior
If:

friction score is high enough

multiple consistent signals exist

hypothesis is coherent

no intermediary-specific signals are present

then classify as:

company_type = operating_company

with a lower-confidence reason if needed

Do NOT return unclear in that scenario.

Rule D — unclear should only be used when evidence is truly insufficient
Use unclear only if:

signals are very sparse

friction score is weak or missing

no meaningful function can be inferred

no company archetype indicators exist at all

🔴 PART 2 — PROTECT FINAL VERDICT FROM DEGRADING
The current system allows this bad behavior:

strong score

strong signals

coherent hypothesis

but final verdict says “Limited data available”

This must be fixed.

New rule
The final_verdict must never be weaker than the strongest available evidence.

If the system already has:
friction_score >= meaningful threshold

repeated signals

coherent hypothesis

then the final verdict should still produce:

a real main pain

a real pain area

a real capability need

a real attack angle

even if company_type confidence is imperfect.

Example behavior
If company_type confidence is weak but business pain is strong:

Display:

Company Type: Likely Operating Company

Reason: No strong evidence suggests this is a staffing or job-market intermediary. Existing signals point to internal growth, analytics investment, and reporting-related pain.

And still produce a strong final verdict.

🔴 PART 3 — UPDATE COMPANY TYPE OUTPUT MODEL
Expand company type output so it includes:

{
  "company_type": "operating_company",
  "analysis_mode": "direct_employer_analysis",
  "target_fit": "primary",
  "company_type_confidence": "medium",
  "company_type_reason": "No strong staffing or recruiting-marketplace indicators were detected. Signals instead suggest internal scaling and business-function pain."
}
Add:

company_type_confidence with values:

high

medium

low

This helps the UI explain classification quality without collapsing into “unclear”.

🔴 PART 4 — ADD FULL RECALCULATION FOR AN EXISTING COMPANY
The product must support rerunning the full pipeline for a company already in the system.

Create a new backend endpoint:

POST /api/v1/companies/{company_id}/recalculate-all
This endpoint should:

load the existing company

run collection again

recompute friction score

regenerate hypothesis

rerun company type detection

regenerate final verdict

return the full updated payload

This should act as a one-click refresh of the company’s full intelligence profile.

Response example
{
  "company": {...},
  "company_type": "operating_company",
  "analysis_mode": "direct_employer_analysis",
  "target_fit": "primary",
  "company_type_confidence": "medium",
  "company_type_reason": "...",
  "signals_count": 18,
  "friction_score": {...},
  "hypothesis": {...},
  "final_verdict": {
    "main_pain": "...",
    "where_pain_lives": "...",
    "what_the_company_needs": "...",
    "best_attack_angle": "..."
  }
}
🔴 PART 5 — FRONTEND: ADD RECALCULATE FULL ANALYSIS ACTION
In the Company Detail page add a prominent action button:

Recalculate Full Analysis
This should:

call POST /api/v1/companies/{company_id}/recalculate-all

show loading state

Thought for 7s
Sí. Aquí ya se ve clarísimo qué está bien y qué todavía está mal.

Primero: qué significa Collection Runs (5)
Eso no significa que Nike tenga 5 problemas ni 5 fuentes distintas.

Significa simplemente:

el sistema analizó esa empresa 5 veces.

Cada fila es una ejecución completa del recolector.
En tu caso, el orchestrator corrió 5 veces y en cada corrida encontró solo 1 señal:

careers page found → https://jobs.nike.com/

O sea, ahora mismo el sistema sabe básicamente esto de Nike:

“Nike tiene página de empleos.”

Nada más.

Por eso Collection Runs (5) se debe leer como:

“He intentado recolectar evidencia 5 veces, y cada vez solo encontré 1 señal.”

Eso en realidad es útil, porque te dice dos cosas:

el pipeline sí está funcionando

pero el collector para Nike está casi ciego

Mi análisis general del resultado de Nike
Lo bueno
Hay 3 cosas bien encaminadas:

1. Company Type
Operating Company tiene sentido.
Nike claramente no es un job board ni una staffing firm.

2. Target Fit
Primary Target también tiene sentido.
NovaWork sí debería analizar empresas como Nike como objetivo principal.

3. La interfaz ya está mucho más entendible
Ya no parece un dashboard técnico puro.
Eso es una mejora real.

Lo malo, y aquí está el problema principal
La salida está contradiciéndose.

Contradicción 1
Dice:

Overall assessment: Low (0.0 / 10)

Limited signs of friction detected

pero luego dice:

“The company is likely struggling…”

“There is a clear opportunity…”

“High confidence…”

“Nike likely has fragmented reporting visibility…”

Eso no puede convivir.

Si solo tienes 1 señal y el score es 0.0, el sistema no puede hablar con tanta seguridad sobre:

data visibility

analytics pain

reporting fragmentation

hiring patterns

capability building

Porque no tiene evidencia para eso.

Qué está pasando realmente
Tu sistema está usando una narrativa heredada de casos como HubSpot, donde sí había señales de:

analytics

reporting

growth

multiple open roles

Pero en Nike no hay eso.
En Nike solo hay:

careers page found

Entonces el sistema está rellenando huecos con texto demasiado ambicioso.

Diagnóstico exacto
Company Type
Está razonablemente bien.

Final Verdict
Está demasiado fuerte para la evidencia disponible.

Opportunity Hypothesis
Está inventando demasiado.

Confidence
Está mal. No debería decir High confidence.

Collection Runs
Te está mostrando, sin querer, el verdadero estado del sistema:

“He corrido varias veces y sigo sin encontrar casi nada.”

Con los datos actuales, el sistema debería decir algo más así:

Company Type
Operating Company

Best next step
Collect deeper signals from careers content, about pages, newsroom, and role descriptions before generating a positioning recommendation.

Eso sería mucho más creíble.

Qué arreglaría ya
1. Regla de consistencia
Si:

score = 0

unique signals <= 2

entonces el sistema no puede producir:

hypothesis fuerte

main pain específico

high confidence

best attack angle agresivo

Debe pasar a modo:

insufficient evidence / preliminary read

2. Confidence real
Tu confianza no debe basarse solo en:

“observed across multiple runs”

Porque aquí el mismo hallazgo se repitió 5 veces.

Eso no significa alta confianza analítica.
Solo significa que el mismo collector encontró lo mismo 5 veces.

La confianza debería considerar:

cantidad de señales únicas

diversidad de fuentes

riqueza semántica

consistencia entre señales

En Nike tienes:

1 señal única

1 tipo de fuente real

0 evidencia funcional específica

Eso es low confidence, no high.

3. Collection Runs debe explicarse mejor
Ahora mismo se ve técnico. Yo lo cambiaría a algo como:

Analysis Attempts: 5
“Five collection attempts were run. So far, the system has only found one consistent signal: an active careers page.”

Eso cualquier humano lo entiende.

4. No generar dolor específico sin evidencia específica
Para decir:

data pain

reporting pain

operations pain

necesitas señales como:

analytics hiring

reporting language

operations roles

revops / supply chain / finance patterns

tool references

newsroom clues

function-specific openings

Si no están, no inventes.

Veredicto honesto sobre este output
¿Va mejor?
Sí, mucho mejor que antes.

¿Ya sirve para decidir a dónde atacar?
Todavía no en este caso de Nike.

Porque el sistema te dice correctamente:

qué tipo de empresa es

pero todavía no te dice con suficiente evidencia cuál es su dolor real.

En HubSpot sonaba mejor porque había más señales.
En Nike, el sistema quedó expuesto: todavía necesita mejor recolección o una regla de prudencia más fuerte.

Lo más importante que te deja este caso
Nike te mostró exactamente lo que faltaba:

no solo necesitas mejores collectors
también necesitas un modo de salida que diga:

“todavía no sé lo suficiente”

Eso también es inteligencia.

Mi recomendación concreta
El siguiente ajuste debe ser este:

si hay poca evidencia, el sistema debe devolver un “Preliminary Verdict” en vez de un “Final Verdict”.

Eso te resolvería gran parte de las contradicciones.

Y sobre Collection Runs (5), quédate con esta frase simple:

Significa que el sistema ha intentado analizar esa empresa 5 veces. En Nike, las 5 corridas encontraron prácticamente la misma única señal, así que todavía no hay suficiente evidencia para un diagnóstico confiable.

Si quieres, te preparo el siguiente prompt para arreglar exactamente eso:
“Evidence Threshold + Preliminary vs Final Verdict Layer”.

🔧 PARTE 4.8.2 — Anti-Hallucination + Evidence Threshold + Output Consistency
You are a senior product engineer improving an internal intelligence system called Friction Radar.

The system already:

collects company signals

computes friction scores

generates hypotheses

classifies company type

renders a final verdict

However, the current behavior has a critical trust problem:

Problem
The system sometimes produces strong conclusions even when evidence is weak.

Example of bad behavior:

friction score is 0.0

only 1 unique signal exists

but the UI still produces:

a strong business pain

a specific functional problem

a confident opportunity statement

high confidence language

This must be fixed.

🎯 PRIMARY OBJECTIVE
Make the system strictly evidence-bound.

The system must:

never invent pain that is not supported by signals

never infer specific functions without enough evidence

never claim high confidence from repeated weak signals

remain internally consistent across:

score

hypothesis

company type

final verdict

🔴 CORE RULE
Do not hallucinate beyond the available evidence.
If the system does not know enough, it must clearly say so.

PART 1 — ADD EVIDENCE THRESHOLD LOGIC
Create a deterministic evidence-threshold layer.

Suggested file:

app/services/evidence_threshold_engine.py

This layer should evaluate:

number of unique signals

number of total signals

number of distinct signal types

number of distinct source types

latest friction score

whether any function-specific signals exist

whether signals are repeated copies of the same observation across runs

Suggested thresholds
High-quality evidence
unique signals >= 4

source types >= 2

friction score > 0

at least 1 function-specific signal exists

e.g. analytics, reporting, operations, recruiting, customer pain

Weak evidence
unique signals <= 2

only one source type

friction score = 0

no function-specific signals

repeated runs only finding the same signal

PART 2 — SPLIT OUTPUT INTO TWO MODES
Replace the current always-on “Final Verdict” behavior with:

A. Preliminary Verdict
Use when evidence is weak.

B. Final Verdict
Use only when evidence passes threshold.

Preliminary Verdict should answer:
what we know

what we do not know yet

what needs to be collected next

Example Preliminary Verdict
What we know: We found a valid careers page, which confirms the company is actively hiring.

What we do not know yet: We do not yet have enough evidence to determine whether the main pain is in data, operations, reporting, or another function.

Next best step: Gather deeper signals from role descriptions, about pages, newsroom content, and function-specific hiring clues before producing a stronger recommendation.

Final Verdict should only appear when evidence is strong enough.
PART 3 — ANTI-HALLUCINATION RULES FOR HYPOTHESIS AND VERDICT
Add these strict rules:

Rule A
If friction score = 0 AND unique signals <= 2:

do NOT generate a strong hypothesis

do NOT assign a specific pain area like data, analytics, reporting, or operations unless directly supported

do NOT show “High confidence”

Rule B
If only generic signals exist such as:

careers page found

newsroom found

homepage exists

general growth language

then output must remain general and cautious.

Rule C
Do not infer:

“data visibility pain”

“reporting fragmentation”

“operations pain”

“recruiting workflow pain”

unless there are explicit supporting signals.

PART 4 — FUNCTION-SPECIFIC INFERENCE RULES
Only infer a pain function if function-specific evidence exists.

Data / analytics / reporting
Require signals such as:

analytics_role_detected

reporting_language_detected

dashboard / metrics / visibility language

business intelligence references

Operations / coordination
Require signals such as:

process_language_detected

operations_role_detected

workflow / efficiency / coordination language

Recruiting / staffing / talent marketplace
Require signals such as:

staffing / recruiting / employers / job seekers / placement language

recruiter workflow signals

candidate matching signals

If function-specific evidence is absent:

say the pain area is not yet clear

PART 5 — CONFIDENCE MUST REFLECT EVIDENCE QUALITY
Current system incorrectly treats repeated identical signals across many runs as “high confidence”.

This is wrong.

Update confidence logic so it depends on:

diversity of unique signals

diversity of source types

function specificity

consistency across runs

friction score strength

Do NOT let:

the same careers-page signal repeated 5 times
produce “High confidence”.

Suggested confidence behavior
High confidence
multiple unique signals

multiple sources

function-specific patterns

coherent score + hypothesis

Medium confidence
some meaningful signals

partial function inference possible

moderate signal diversity

Low confidence
few unique signals

mostly generic signals

score low or zero

no clear function inference

PART 6 — FIX INTERNAL CONTRADICTIONS
Prevent outputs like:

low score

no meaningful matched signals

but strong final verdict

Create a consistency guard:

If top-level evidence is weak:

downgrade hypothesis strength

downgrade verdict strength

downgrade confidence

switch to Preliminary Verdict mode

PART 7 — IMPROVE COLLECTION RUNS PRESENTATION
Current “Collection Runs (5)” is too technical.

Rename this section in the UI to:

Analysis Attempts
Also add a human explanation above the table, such as:

The system has analyzed this company 5 times. So far, it has found only 1 consistent signal.

or

Multiple analysis attempts found the same small set of signals, which means current evidence is still limited.

Important rule
Repeated runs should not be treated as richer evidence unless they produce new unique signals.

PART 8 — RAW SIGNALS SHOULD BE INTERPRETED HONESTLY
If only one signal exists, such as:

Careers Page Found

then the system should say something like:

We confirmed that the company is hiring, but we do not yet have enough evidence to determine the specific business pain behind that hiring.

This is preferable to inventing a business thesis.

PART 9 — UPDATE NIKE-LIKE BEHAVIOR
For a company like Nike, if the system only finds:

careers page found
and nothing else meaningful,

the output should look like:

Company Type
Operating Company

Confidence
Low

Verdict Type
Preliminary Verdict

What we know
The company has an active careers page, which suggests active hiring.

What we do not know yet
We do not yet have enough evidence to identify whether the main pain is in data, operations, reporting, or another area.

Next best step
Collect deeper signals from job descriptions, about content, newsroom content, and function-specific hiring language before generating a stronger recommendation.

This is the correct behavior.

PART 10 — FRONTEND CHANGES
Update the Company Detail page so that the top business section can show either:

Final Verdict
or

Preliminary Verdict

depending on evidence quality.

Also display:

Confidence

Evidence quality

Analysis attempts summary

PART 11 — RESPONSE MODEL UPDATES
Add fields such as:

{
  "verdict_type": "preliminary",
  "evidence_quality": "low",
  "confidence": "low",
  "what_we_know": "...",
  "what_we_do_not_know_yet": "...",
  "next_best_step": "..."
}
And for stronger cases:

{
  "verdict_type": "final",
  "evidence_quality": "high",
  "confidence": "medium",
  "main_pain": "...",
  "where_pain_lives": "...",
  "what_the_company_needs": "...",
  "best_attack_angle": "..."
}
PART 12 — DO NOT BREAK EXISTING GOOD CASES
For companies like HubSpot, where the system already has:

multiple unique signals

repeated evidence

function-specific hints

meaningful score

the system should still produce a Final Verdict.

This anti-hallucination layer should suppress weak cases, not weaken strong ones.

CONSTRAINTS
do not add external AI services

do not rebuild the app

do not remove existing analysis pipeline

do not over-design the UI

keep everything deterministic and evidence-based

EXPECTED OUTPUT
Return:

evidence threshold logic

verdict mode logic (preliminary vs final)

anti-hallucination consistency rules

confidence recalculation logic

updated company detail UI behavior

improved “Analysis Attempts” wording

sample output for weak-evidence companies like Nike

sample output for stronger-evidence companies like HubSpot

Optimize for:

trust

honesty

internal consistency

business usefulness

Qué espero que cambie después de esto
Para Nike, con la evidencia actual, el sistema ya no debería decir:

“The company is likely struggling to maintain clear visibility across data…”

“High confidence…”

“There is a clear opportunity…”

Debería decir algo como:

Preliminary Verdict
We know Nike is actively hiring.

We do not yet know enough to identify the main business pain.

More function-specific evidence is needed before a positioning recommendation can be trusted.

Y para HubSpot, si sí hay señales suficientes, debe seguir mostrando un Final Verdict útil.

Si quieres, después de aplicar esto, el siguiente paso natural es endurecer los collectors para que Nike y empresas parecidas dejen de quedarse en modo preliminar.

Thought for 4s
Perfecto. Vamos a hacer un ajuste quirúrgico para que la pantalla deje de contradecirse.

El objetivo de este prompt es simple:

si la evidencia es débil,
todo el sistema debe comportarse como preliminary

🔧 PARTE 4.8.3 — Preliminary Mode Consistency + Hypothesis Downgrade
Writing
You are a senior product engineer improving an internal intelligence system called Friction Radar.

The system already supports:

company analysis

signal collection

friction scoring

company type detection

preliminary vs final verdict modes

However, there is still a major product problem:

Problem
The top of the page correctly switches to Preliminary Verdict when evidence is weak, but lower sections still behave as if the system has strong evidence.

This creates contradictions such as:

Preliminary Verdict says evidence is low

friction score is 0.0

only 1 unique signal exists

but the page still shows:

a specific primary challenge

a strong functional pain area

a strong opportunity hypothesis

high confidence

assertive “full analysis” language

This must be fixed.

🎯 PRIMARY GOAL
Make the entire page obey the same evidence standard.

If the company is in preliminary mode, then:

all downstream insight blocks must also be preliminary

no strong hypothesis should be shown

no function-specific pain should be inferred without evidence

no strong confidence language should appear

The entire UI must remain internally consistent.

🔴 PART 1 — GLOBAL VERDICT MODE CONTROL
Create a single top-level verdict mode state that controls downstream rendering:

verdict_type
preliminary

final

This should be determined once from the evidence-threshold logic and then reused across the whole page.

Do NOT let each section independently invent its own strength level.

Rule
If verdict_type = preliminary, then the following sections must either:

switch to preliminary variants

or be hidden

or be downgraded

Affected sections:

Primary Challenge

Opportunity Hypothesis

Where the problem likely exists

What the real problem is

Why they are likely hiring

Where you can add value

Who would be valuable here

If you were targeting this company

Full analysis

Confidence messaging

🔴 PART 2 — PRIMARY CHALLENGE MUST NOT FAKE SPECIFICITY
Current bad behavior:

score = 0

breakdown = all 0

but UI still shows “Primary challenge: Reporting Fragmentation”

This must stop.

New rule
If all category scores are 0 or no category meaningfully stands out:

show:

Primary Challenge
Not enough evidence yet

or

No clear challenge identified yet

Do NOT force a challenge label when no challenge is supported.

🔴 PART 3 — PRELIMINARY HYPOTHESIS MODE
When verdict_type = preliminary, replace the current strong hypothesis block with a reduced version.

Rename section:

Opportunity Hypothesis → Preliminary Read
This block should include only:

1. What we know
Short statement grounded in actual signals only.

2. What we do not know yet
Explicitly state that the specific function or pain area is still unclear.

3. What we need next
Describe what additional evidence would help.

Example for Nike-like case
Preliminary Read

What we know
We confirmed that the company has an active careers page, which suggests active hiring.

What we do not know yet
We do not yet have enough evidence to determine whether the main pain is in data, operations, reporting, supply chain, recruiting, or another function.

What we need next
We need more signals from job descriptions, about content, newsroom content, and role-specific language before generating a stronger recommendation.

Important rule
In preliminary mode, do NOT show:

“The company is likely struggling with…”

“There is a clear opportunity…”

“Who would be valuable here…”

“If you were targeting this company…”
unless directly supported by strong evidence.

🔴 PART 4 — HIDE OR DOWNGRADE STRONG SECTIONS IN PRELIMINARY MODE
When verdict is preliminary, apply these behaviors:

Hide entirely:
Who would be valuable here

If you were targeting this company

Replace with softer wording:
Where the problem likely exists → “Problem area not clear yet”

What the real problem is → “Main problem not yet identifiable”

Why they are likely hiring → “Hiring confirmed, but underlying pain not yet clear”

Where you can add value → “Positioning recommendation not ready yet”

Full analysis
Replace with:
Internal note
“This company currently has limited evidence. A stronger analysis requires more function-specific signals.”

🔴 PART 5 — CONFIDENCE MUST MATCH MODE
If verdict_type = preliminary, then confidence cannot be high unless there is genuinely strong evidence.

Rule
If:

friction score = 0

unique signals <= 2

no function-specific signals

one repeated generic signal across many runs

then:

confidence = low
Replace wording
Instead of:
“High confidence - we observed consistent patterns across multiple sources.”

Use:
“Low confidence - current evidence is limited and does not yet point clearly to a specific business function or pain area.”

🔴 PART 6 — ANALYSIS ATTEMPTS SHOULD EXPLAIN LIMITATION
Keep the section renamed as:

Analysis Attempts
Add a summary line above it, generated from evidence state.

Weak evidence example:
“The system analyzed this company 7 times. So far, it has only found one consistent signal: an active careers page.”

Strong evidence example:
“Multiple analysis attempts found several consistent signals across different sources.”

This section should help explain why a verdict is preliminary.

🔴 PART 7 — DO NOT CONFUSE REPEATED SIGNALS WITH NEW EVIDENCE
If the same single signal appears across many runs, treat it as:

consistency of that signal
not

broader evidence richness

The UI should communicate:

repeated confirmation

but still limited breadth

🔴 PART 8 — FRONTEND RENDERING RULES
Update the Company Detail page so rendering is controlled by verdict_type.

If verdict_type = final
Show:

Final Verdict

Primary Challenge

Opportunity Hypothesis

Where you can add value

Who would be valuable here

If you were targeting this company

If verdict_type = preliminary
Show:

Preliminary Verdict

Primary Challenge = not enough evidence yet

Preliminary Read

Confidence = low/medium as appropriate

Next best step

Analysis Attempts summary

Hide or soften strong downstream sections.

🔴 PART 9 — RESPONSE MODEL ADDITIONS
Ensure the backend response includes enough fields for rendering consistency:

{
  "verdict_type": "preliminary",
  "evidence_quality": "low",
  "confidence": "low",
  "primary_challenge_label": null,
  "preliminary_read": {
    "what_we_know": "...",
    "what_we_do_not_know_yet": "...",
    "what_we_need_next": "..."
  },
  "analysis_attempts_summary": "The system analyzed this company 7 times. So far, it has only found one consistent signal: an active careers page."
}
For final mode, existing richer fields can remain.

Expected top-of-page behavior:

🚨 CONSTRAINTS
do not rebuild the app

sample output for weak-evidence and strong-evidence cases

business usefulness
