Prompt 5.0 — Job Description Intelligence + Function Inference
You are a senior backend engineer and intelligence system designer improving an internal product called Friction Radar.

The system already:

creates companies

collects basic public signals

computes friction scores

generates hypotheses

classifies company type

supports preliminary vs final verdicts

The current limitation is clear:

Problem
For many companies, especially large operating companies like Nike, the collectors only find generic signals such as:

careers page found

newsroom found

homepage growth language

This is not enough to identify:

where the real pain likely lives

what function is under pressure

what type of candidate or capability should be positioned

The system now needs a deeper intelligence layer focused on job descriptions and function inference.

PRIMARY GOAL
Upgrade collection and analysis so the system can answer:

What functional areas is this company actively hiring for?

What repeated needs appear across job descriptions?

What likely business pain does that hiring imply?

What capability should NovaWork position against that pain?

PART 1 — JOB DESCRIPTION DISCOVERY
Extend the collectors so they do not stop at finding the careers page.

The system should now:

discover the careers/jobs page

extract visible job listing links where possible

open a limited number of role pages

parse job titles and job description text

persist structured role-level signals

Keep this practical and lightweight for MVP.

Do NOT build a massive crawler.

Scope limits
For each company:

inspect up to 10–20 visible job listings max

prefer recent / visible / high-signal roles

stop early if enough useful evidence is found

PART 2 — NEW ROLE-LEVEL DATA MODEL
Add structured storage for job role intelligence.

Create tables such as:

company_job_roles
id

company_id

source_url

role_title

role_location

role_department_raw

role_description_text

discovered_at

created_at

company_role_signals
id

company_id

job_role_id

signal_type

signal_text

functional_area

confidence

created_at

Use practical naming and keep it compatible with the current schema style.

PART 3 — FUNCTIONAL AREA INFERENCE
Add a new deterministic inference layer that classifies each role into a functional area.

Create a service such as:

app/services/function_inference_engine.py

For each job title and description, infer one primary functional area:

functional_area options
data_analytics

business_intelligence

finance

accounting

operations

supply_chain

logistics

marketing

sales

customer_success

product

engineering

unknown

Signals like:

analyst

Signals like:

Signals like:

Do this deterministically with keyword families and simple scoring.

PART 4 — JOB SIGNAL EXTRACTION
From job titles and descriptions, extract richer role-level signals such as:

analytics_hiring_detected

dashboarding_detected

recruiting_hiring_detected

cross_functional_language_detected

systems_tooling_language_detected

These signals should be stronger than generic homepage/careers signals.

Persist them and connect them to the company.

PART 5 — HIRING PATTERN SUMMARY
Build a summary layer that answers:

Hiring Patterns
which functions are hiring most

how often each function appears

which role families dominate

what capability themes repeat

Example output:

{
  "top_functional_areas": [
    {"area": "supply_chain", "count": 4},
    {"area": "operations", "count": 3},
    {"area": "data_analytics", "count": 2}
  ],
  "top_capability_themes": [
    "planning",
    "reporting",
    "cross-functional coordination"
  ]
}
This should become a major evidence source for verdict generation.

PART 6 — PAIN INFERENCE FROM HIRING PATTERNS
Use repeated function-specific hiring to infer likely pain.

Examples:

If repeated roles appear in:
analytics

BI

reporting

dashboards

Infer likely pain around:

reporting clarity

business visibility

decision support

metrics alignment

If repeated roles appear in:
supply chain

planning

logistics

inventory

Infer likely pain around:

operational visibility

planning complexity

coordination across fulfillment/distribution

supply chain pressure

If repeated roles appear in:
operations

process improvement

workflow

Infer likely pain around:

scaling operations

process inconsistency

coordination inefficiency

If repeated roles appear in:
recruiting

sourcing

talent acquisition

Infer likely pain around:

hiring operations

talent pipeline management

recruiting workflow efficiency

This inference should be stronger than generic “the company is growing”.

PART 7 — UPGRADE FINAL VERDICT WITH FUNCTIONAL EVIDENCE
Update the final verdict engine so it prefers job-description evidence over generic homepage evidence.

If role-level evidence exists, the verdict should use that first.

Example:

Instead of:
“The company is growing quickly and may face coordination challenges.”

Use:
“The company is actively hiring across supply chain planning and operations roles, which suggests pressure around operational visibility and coordination as the business scales.”

Then derive:

main pain

where the pain lives

what the company likely needs

best attack angle

from role-level evidence.

PART 8 — PRELIMINARY VS FINAL SHOULD DEPEND ON ROLE EVIDENCE TOO
A company should move from Preliminary Verdict to Final Verdict when role-level evidence becomes strong enough.

Example:
If the system finds:

5 job descriptions

3 repeated roles in analytics / reporting

strong function-specific signals

then it should be allowed to produce a Final Verdict even if homepage signals were weak.

PART 9 — NEW UI SECTIONS
Update the company detail page to include a new section above raw signals:

Hiring Intelligence
Show:

top functional areas hiring

top repeated capability themes

role titles sampled

function inference confidence

Example:

Hiring Intelligence
Top area hiring: Supply Chain

Secondary area: Operations

Repeated themes: planning, cross-functional coordination, reporting

Sample roles:

Supply Chain Analyst

Inventory Planning Manager

Operations Excellence Lead

This should be much more useful than generic “careers page found”.

PART 10 — SUPPORTING UI FOR WEAK CASES
If no job listings or descriptions can be parsed, say so clearly.

Example:
“We found the careers page, but were not able to extract enough role-level detail yet.”

Do not pretend to know more than the evidence allows.

PART 11 — COLLECTION STRATEGY RULES
When possible:

prioritize job titles first

then inspect descriptions

stop once enough function-specific evidence is found

Avoid:

deep crawling

scraping hundreds of pages

overly brittle extraction logic

Optimize for:

useful evidence fast

not perfect completeness

PART 12 — OUTPUT EXPECTATIONS
Return:

updated collector design

new database schema for role-level data

role parsing logic

functional area inference logic

job-level signal extraction logic

hiring pattern summary logic

updated final verdict logic using hiring evidence

updated company detail UI section for Hiring Intelligence

example outputs for:

Nike-like operating company

recruiting intermediary

weak-evidence company

FINAL GOAL
After this upgrade, the system should be able to say things like:

“This company is hiring heavily in supply chain planning and operations, suggesting pain in operational visibility and coordination.”

“This company is hiring across analytics and reporting roles, suggesting a need for clearer business intelligence and decision support.”

“This company is mainly hiring recruiting and talent roles, suggesting pressure in hiring workflow and candidate pipeline operations.”

The system should move from:

“they are hiring”

to:

“they are hiring in this function, which suggests this business pain, which points to this opportunity.”
end

Debería aspirar a algo como:

Thought for 18s
Exacto. No es que no haya evidencia.
Lo que hay es un problema de extracción.

Tú, como humano, ya viste evidencia fuerte en esa página:

930 open positions

áreas visibles como Retail, Distribution, Manufacturing

títulos reales de puestos

ubicaciones

botones de View Job

Entonces el problema no es:

“Nike no tiene suficiente evidencia”
El problema es:

“Friction Radar todavía no está leyendo esa evidencia”
Qué está pasando realmente
Tu sistema hoy solo logró extraer:

careers page found

Pero la página de Nike claramente contiene mucho más.

Eso normalmente pasa por una de estas razones:

1. La página carga los trabajos con JavaScript
El HTML inicial que ve tu scraper puede venir casi vacío, y los puestos se renderizan después en el navegador.

2. El collector no está esperando lo suficiente
Encuentra el link de careers y se detiene antes de que aparezcan:

job cards

total open positions

categorías

botones de view job

3. El selector del scraper está mal o muy genérico
La UI sí ve:

“OPEN POSITIONS: 930”

tabs de áreas

cards de empleos

pero el scraper no está leyendo esos nodos.

4. El sitio puede tener protección ligera o estructura dinámica
Muchos career sites usan componentes JS, APIs internas o navegación dinámica.

Tu intuición es correcta
Con esa captura, yo no aceptaría que el sistema diga:

“insufficient evidence”

Yo diría:

hay evidencia visible para humanos, pero el collector no la está capturando todavía.
Eso es muy distinto.

Qué debería decir el sistema mientras tanto
Hasta que el collector mejore, en vez de decir:

“Not enough evidence”

debería decir algo como:

“Machine extraction is still limited for this careers site, even though visible hiring evidence exists.”
o más simple:

“We can see visible hiring activity on the careers site, but the system has not yet extracted enough structured role data.”
Eso sería honesto y mucho más correcto.

Lo que ya puedes inferir manualmente de esa pantalla
Sin siquiera entrar a los job descriptions, ya hay señales útiles:

1. Volumen de hiring alto
930 posiciones abiertas no es una señal menor.
Eso sugiere actividad de contratación significativa.

2. Áreas visibles de hiring
Ya ves categorías:

Retail

Distribution

Manufacturing

Eso ya apunta a funciones reales del negocio.

3. Roles visibles
Ejemplos:

Retail Associate

Department Manager

Eso ya te dice que, al menos en esa vista, la presión visible está muy ligada a:

retail operations

store staffing

frontline execution

Lo importante para NovaWork
Con solo esa pantalla, el sistema ya debería poder moverse de:

“solo careers page found”
a algo más útil como:

Hiring Intelligence
High visible hiring volume detected

Hiring appears concentrated in retail and frontline operations

Additional categories suggest distribution and manufacturing demand

Preliminary functional read
likely pressure in retail operations staffing

possible broader demand across distribution and manufacturing

Eso sí empieza a servir.

El problema técnico exacto a resolver
Tu collector necesita dejar de hacer esto:

encontrar careers URL

guardar un solo signal

terminar

Y empezar a hacer esto:

Paso 1
Abrir la página con navegador real o Playwright

Paso 2
Esperar a que carguen elementos visibles como:

total positions

job cards

category tabs

Paso 3
Extraer:

total positions count

category names

first 10–20 job cards

titles

locations

department/category if visible

job URLs

Qué señales nuevas deberías guardar para Nike

high_open_positions_count_detected

distribution_hiring_detected

manufacturing_hiring_detected

frontline_store_roles_detected

Y eso cambia todo.

Preliminary Verdict
We found strong visible hiring activity, including a high number of open positions and hiring categories across retail, distribution, and manufacturing. This suggests that Nike may be experiencing staffing and operational pressure in frontline and fulfillment-related functions, though deeper role-level analysis is still needed before identifying the exact business pain.

Eso ya está muchísimo mejor que “solo hay careers page”.

Mi conclusión clara
No estás frente a falta de evidencia.
Estás frente a:

falta de extracción estructurada de evidencia visible
Y eso es bueno, porque significa que el valor sí está ahí.

Qué haría yo ahora mismo
1. Cambiar el wording del sistema
Para que no diga “no evidence” cuando sí hay evidencia visible no extraída.

2. Mejorar el collector de career pages dinámicas
Especialmente para:

total openings

category tabs

job cards

first-level role metadata

3. Usar esa metadata para inferencia funcional inicial
Aunque todavía no tengas full job description parsing.

Veredicto final sobre Nike
Tu caso de Nike te está mostrando esto:

El sistema ya no necesita más copy.
Necesita un collector más inteligente para páginas de careers dinámicas.

Ese es el verdadero siguiente paso.

Puedo prepararte el prompt exacto para ese arreglo: un sprint 5.1 solo para dynamic careers extraction en páginas como Nike.

Thought for a few seconds
Perfecto. Vamos a hacer un prompt quirúrgico para resolver exactamente el problema de Nike:

el sistema sí encuentra la página de careers,
pero no está extrayendo la evidencia visible que ya existe en pantalla.

Este prompt va enfocado solo en eso.

Prompt 5.1 — Dynamic Careers Extraction for Modern Job Pages
You are a senior scraping engineer and product intelligence engineer improving an internal system called Friction Radar.

The system already:

finds company careers pages

stores generic signals

computes friction scores

generates preliminary/final verdicts

However, there is a critical limitation:

Problem
For modern careers sites like Nike, the system can detect the careers page but fails to extract visible evidence that is clearly present to a human user, such as:

total number of open positions

visible hiring categories

job cards

visible job titles

visible locations

visible department / area labels

“View Job” links

As a result, the product incorrectly behaves as if evidence is weak, when in reality the page contains strong visible hiring evidence that the collector is simply not extracting.

This must be fixed.

PRIMARY GOAL
Upgrade the careers collector so that for dynamic job pages (especially JS-rendered ones), the system can extract visible structured hiring evidence even before full job description parsing succeeds.

The collector should move beyond:

careers page found

and begin extracting:

hiring volume

visible function areas

visible job titles

visible locations

visible categories

visible job links

PART 1 — TARGET USE CASE
Use a company like Nike as the reference case.

Example observed visible evidence:

“OPEN POSITIONS: 930”

category tabs such as:

Retail

Distribution

Manufacturing

visible job cards

role titles

locations

“View Job” buttons

The collector must be able to extract this type of evidence from the rendered page.

PART 2 — DYNAMIC PAGE EXTRACTION STRATEGY
Implement or improve a collector specifically for dynamic careers pages.

Suggested file:

app/collectors/dynamic_careers.py

Use browser automation (Playwright) for these pages.

Required behavior
The collector should:

open the careers page in a real browser context

wait for visible content to render

detect whether job cards or hiring content appear

extract visible structured evidence

persist new signals even if full role detail extraction is not yet possible

Important
Do NOT stop collection after finding only the careers link.

The collector must attempt to read the page contents after navigation.

PART 3 — WHAT TO EXTRACT FROM THE CAREERS PAGE
Extract the following when visible:

A. Hiring volume
Examples:

“Open Positions: 930”

total jobs count

result count

Store as signals like:

high_open_positions_count_detected

open_positions_count_detected

Include numeric value where possible.

B. Visible hiring categories / tabs / departments
Examples:

Retail

Distribution

Manufacturing

Engineering

Corporate

Technology

Supply Chain

Store signals like:

retail_hiring_detected

distribution_hiring_detected

manufacturing_hiring_detected

engineering_hiring_detected

Also store normalized category names.

C. Visible job cards
For visible listings on the page, extract:

role title

location

department/category label if visible

job link if visible

Persist these into company_job_roles or equivalent.

D. “View Job” URLs
If visible, capture the job detail URLs for later parsing.

Even if the detail page is not parsed yet, this is useful evidence.

PART 4 — PAGE INTERACTION RULES
Modern career pages may require light interaction.

Support:

waiting for network idle and visible selectors

scrolling if needed

reading visible tabs/categories

optionally clicking or reading the first category tabs if cheap and reliable

Do NOT build a brittle full crawler.

Do NOT scrape hundreds of jobs.

Optimize for:

first useful visible evidence

speed

robustness

Suggested extraction target
Extract:

page-level evidence

first 10–20 visible job cards max

first few visible categories/tabs

That is enough for MVP.

PART 5 — NEW SIGNAL TYPES TO ADD
Add support for signals like:

open_positions_count_detected

high_open_positions_count_detected

job_cards_visible_detected

retail_hiring_detected

distribution_hiring_detected

manufacturing_hiring_detected

supply_chain_hiring_detected

store_operations_hiring_detected

frontline_roles_detected

job_location_patterns_detected

job_links_extracted

Keep naming consistent with the rest of the system.

PART 6 — FUNCTIONAL INFERENCE FROM VISIBLE JOB DATA
Even before deep job description parsing, infer preliminary hiring areas from visible job cards and categories.

Examples:

If visible jobs are:
Retail Associate

Department Manager

Store Lead

Infer:

retail_operations

frontline_staffing

If categories include:
Distribution

Manufacturing

Infer:

supply_chain

manufacturing_operations

This should feed the hiring intelligence layer.

PART 7 — HIRING INTELLIGENCE UPGRADE
Update the Hiring Intelligence section so it can render page-level evidence such as:

Open positions count

Top visible hiring categories

Sample visible roles

Sample visible locations

Example output:

Visible hiring volume: 930 open positions

Top visible hiring areas: Retail, Distribution, Manufacturing

Sample visible roles:

Retail Associate

Department Manager

Sample locations:

St. Louis, Missouri

Berkeley, California

Zapopan, Jalisco

This is far more useful than “careers page found”.

PART 8 — PRELIMINARY VERDICT SHOULD USE VISIBLE CAREERS EVIDENCE
If the system extracts:

high open positions count

multiple visible hiring categories

multiple visible role titles

then the company should no longer behave like a “single-signal weak case”.

Even if full job descriptions are not parsed yet, the verdict can upgrade from:

extremely weak evidence

to:

meaningful preliminary evidence

Example improved preliminary verdict:
“We found strong visible hiring activity, including a high volume of open positions and multiple hiring categories such as retail, distribution, and manufacturing. This suggests operational demand across frontline and fulfillment-related functions, though deeper role-level analysis is still needed to isolate the exact pain point.”

PART 9 — COLLECTOR DESIGN REQUIREMENTS
The collector should be modular and resilient.

Implement:

clear selectors strategy

fallback selectors

timeout handling

screenshots/logging for failed extraction if useful

graceful fallback if only some page elements are found

If the collector can find:

open positions count
but not job cards,
it should still persist the count signal.

If it can find:

job cards
but not category tabs,
it should still persist the role signals.

Partial extraction is acceptable and valuable.

PART 10 — PREVENT FALSE “LOW EVIDENCE” STATES
Update evidence evaluation so that these page-level signals count as meaningful evidence:

high open position count

multiple visible hiring categories

multiple visible job cards

multiple distinct role titles

This should help prevent false weak-mode outputs for companies like Nike.

PART 11 — FRONTEND DISPLAY CHANGES
Update the company detail page so Hiring Intelligence can show page-level extraction results clearly.

Suggested display:

Hiring Intelligence
Visible hiring volume: 930 open positions

Top visible hiring areas: Retail, Distribution, Manufacturing

Sample visible roles:

Retail Associate

Department Manager

Evidence quality: Moderate

If only partial page evidence was extracted, say so clearly.

PART 12 — EXPECTED OUTPUT
Return:

updated dynamic careers collector design

Playwright-based extraction flow

selector/fallback strategy

new page-level signal types

job-card extraction logic

visible category extraction logic

updated hiring intelligence logic

evidence-threshold adjustment for visible careers evidence

sample output for Nike-like careers pages

Optimize for:

useful structured evidence fast

robustness on JS-rendered pages

better function inference

improved NovaWork targeting value

FINAL GOAL
After this upgrade, the system should be able to say something like:

“Visible hiring activity is high, with 930 open positions and hiring categories across retail, distribution, and manufacturing. This suggests broad operational demand, especially in frontline and fulfillment-related functions.”

Instead of only:

“Careers page found.”

Qué deberías esperar después de esto
Si esto sale bien, Nike debería pasar de:

1 señal única

evidencia muy pobre

a algo como:

hiring volume alto

áreas visibles de contratación

roles concretos

mejor preliminary verdict

mucho mejor pista de por dónde atacar

Lo que yo probaría apenas lo implementen
Haz estas pruebas:

nike.com

maersk.com

roberthalf.com

Y revisa si ya puede distinguir:

volumen real de contratación

función visible

intermediario laboral vs empresa operadora

Cuando lo tengas, te ayudo a revisar si ya empieza a decirte dónde atacar de verdad.

Sí. Vamos a cerrarlo bien.

Lo que te está pasando es que has iterado sobre síntomas, pero no has hecho un cambio de modelo.
La corrección definitiva es esta:

Ya no uses un solo score para todo.
Separa obligatoriamente:

1. Hiring Pressure
Qué tan fuerte es la señal de contratación visible.

2. Pain Clarity
Qué tan claro está el dolor específico.

Con eso se acaba la contradicción de casos como Nike:

Hiring Pressure: High

Pain Clarity: Low

Eso sí es coherente.

Qué debe desaparecer
Eliminar o reemplazar estas salidas cuando no haya evidencia suficiente:

“The company appears to be operating smoothly.”

“Primary challenge: Process Inefficiency”

cualquier dolor específico si no hay evidencia funcional real

cualquier hipótesis de data/reporting/ops si solo hay evidencia amplia de hiring

Regla definitiva del producto
Si hay:
muchas vacantes

áreas visibles

roles visibles

pero NO hay:

títulos repetidos por familia funcional

job descriptions parseadas

evidencia fuerte de una función específica

entonces el sistema debe decir:

Hiring Pressure = High
Pain Clarity = Low
Diagnosis Status = Broad hiring pattern detected
Primary Pain = Not isolated yet
Y punto.

Prompt definitivo
Prompt 5.2 — Definitive Separation of Hiring Pressure vs Pain Clarity
You are a senior product architect and intelligence system designer making a final corrective pass on an internal system called Friction Radar.

This is not a minor refinement.

This is a definitive model correction.

The system has gone through too many iterations that still produce contradictory outputs.

Your job is to fix the product logic at the root.

PRIMARY PRODUCT PROBLEM
The system currently mixes two different things into one result:

visible hiring demand

clarity of the internal business pain

This creates bad outputs such as:

a company with 930 visible open positions being labeled “Low”

the UI saying “operating smoothly”

a specific pain label being forced when the system does not yet know the real pain

broad hiring evidence being incorrectly treated as weak evidence

generic or hallucinated pain being shown too early

This must stop.

FINAL MODEL CHANGE (NON-NEGOTIABLE)
Replace the old single-layer interpretation with these two separate dimensions:

1. Hiring Pressure
Measures:

how strong the hiring signal is

how much visible demand exists

how broad the hiring activity appears to be

2. Pain Clarity
Measures:

how clearly the system can identify the specific internal pain

whether the company’s real problem has been isolated

whether there is enough function-level evidence to recommend a precise attack angle

These two dimensions must be displayed separately and must drive all downstream output.

This is mandatory.

PART 1 — REMOVE OLD MISLEADING LOGIC
Stop using the existing “Friction Score” as the top-level truth.

Do NOT let the product imply:

“Low activity”

“Operating smoothly”

“Primary challenge: X”

when the real situation is:

hiring pressure is high

but pain clarity is low

If the old friction score still exists internally, demote it to a secondary diagnostic metric only.

It must NOT define the top-level business output alone.

PART 2 — INTRODUCE TWO TOP-LEVEL BUSINESS SCORES
Create and display:

Hiring Pressure
Possible values:

Low

Moderate

High

Pain Clarity
Possible values:

Low

Moderate

High

Hiring Pressure should be based on signals like:
open positions count

visible hiring categories

number of visible job cards

number of visible roles

number of distinct functional areas hiring

repeated hiring evidence across roles

Pain Clarity should be based on signals like:
number of parsed job titles

number of parsed job descriptions

repeated function-specific role families

strong functional inference

strong role-level signals

clear dominant function pattern

PART 3 — DEFINITIVE LOGIC RULES
These rules are non-negotiable:

Rule A
High hiring volume does NOT equal identified pain.

Rule B
Broad hiring evidence must not be labeled “Low” just because the pain is not yet isolated.

Rule C
If hiring pressure is high but pain clarity is low, the product must explicitly say:

“Broad hiring pattern detected; specific pain not yet isolated.”
Rule D
If pain clarity is low, do NOT force:

primary challenge

strong attack angle

specific function diagnosis

strong capability recommendation

Rule E
The UI must never say “operating smoothly” when visible hiring pressure is high.

That phrase should be removed entirely from weak-clarity but high-demand cases.

PART 4 — NEW TOP-LEVEL OUTPUT STATE
Add a new top-level section near the top of the page:

Business Read
This should include:

Hiring Pressure

Pain Clarity

Diagnosis Status

Diagnosis Status options
broad_hiring_pattern_detected

specific_pain_emerging

specific_pain_identified

insufficient_evidence

Example for Nike-like case
Hiring Pressure
High

Pain Clarity
Low

Diagnosis Status
Broad hiring pattern detected

Human explanation
“The company shows strong visible hiring activity across multiple functions, but the system does not yet have enough role-level evidence to isolate the main internal pain.”

PART 5 — NEW RULE FOR PRIMARY CHALLENGE
Do NOT show “Primary Challenge” unless Pain Clarity is at least Moderate.

If Pain Clarity is Low, replace that entire field with:

Current Diagnosis
Broad hiring pattern detected
or

Not enough evidence to isolate the main pain yet

This prevents fake specificity.

PART 6 — FINAL VERDICT MUST DEPEND ON PAIN CLARITY
Update final verdict logic:

If Hiring Pressure = High AND Pain Clarity = Low
Do NOT produce a definitive pain statement.

Instead output:

What we know
The company is hiring visibly and broadly across multiple areas.

What this suggests
There is meaningful organizational demand, but the main pain has not yet been isolated.

What we need next
More role-level evidence is needed from job titles and job descriptions.

NovaWork implication
This is worth tracking, but not yet precise enough for a highly targeted positioning strategy.

If Hiring Pressure = High AND Pain Clarity = Moderate/High
Then the system may produce:

main pain

where pain lives

what company needs

best attack angle

Only then.

PART 7 — NIKE SHOULD BE THE REFERENCE TEST CASE
For Nike-like output, the system should no longer say:

“Low”

“Operating smoothly”

“Process Inefficiency”

“Data/reporting pain”

“Clear opportunity to fix analytics”

unless role-level evidence truly supports those conclusions.

Instead, the expected correct output should be:

Hiring Pressure
High

Pain Clarity
Low

Diagnosis Status
Broad hiring pattern detected

What we know
Visible hiring activity is strong, with a high number of open roles and multiple visible hiring areas such as retail, distribution, manufacturing, and operations.

What we do not know yet
We do not yet know which specific internal function is under the most pressure.

Next best step
Parse job titles and role descriptions to identify repeated functional demand and isolate the strongest business pain.

This is the correct behavior.

PART 8 — HIRING INTELLIGENCE MUST BECOME PRIMARY EVIDENCE
Promote the Hiring Intelligence section.

It should now drive the business read more than generic friction logic.

For example, if the system sees:

930 open positions

visible categories like Retail, Distribution, Manufacturing

visible role cards

it should produce a strong Hiring Pressure result even if Pain Clarity remains low.

PART 9 — FRONTEND CHANGES
Update the top of the Company Detail page to render in this order:

Company Summary

Company Type

Business Read

Hiring Pressure

Pain Clarity

Diagnosis Status

Hiring Intelligence

Verdict / Recommendation block

Supporting evidence

Secondary diagnostic metrics

Raw signals

Analysis attempts

Do NOT put old friction logic above the new business interpretation.

PART 10 — DEMOTE OR REMOVE BAD LANGUAGE
Remove or replace the following phrases in weak-clarity cases:

“The company appears to be operating smoothly”

“Primary challenge: Process Inefficiency”

“The company is likely struggling with reporting...”

“The company is likely struggling with data visibility...”

any specific pain that is not clearly evidenced

These phrases damage trust and must be removed.

PART 11 — RESPONSE MODEL CHANGES
Return fields like:

{
  "hiring_pressure": "high",
  "pain_clarity": "low",
  "diagnosis_status": "broad_hiring_pattern_detected",
  "business_read_summary": "The company shows strong visible hiring activity across multiple functions, but the system does not yet have enough role-level evidence to isolate the main pain.",
  "next_best_step": "Parse more job titles and descriptions to isolate the strongest function-level pressure."
}
If Pain Clarity becomes high later, then richer verdict fields can appear.

PART 12 — UX REQUIREMENT
The system must help the user answer:

“Is this company under visible talent pressure?”
and separately:

“Do we already know where the pain is?”
Those are different questions, and the UI must reflect that clearly.

PART 13 — EXPECTED OUTPUT
Return:

updated backend logic for Hiring Pressure and Pain Clarity

diagnosis status rules

updated final verdict rules

updated Company Detail UI structure

wording replacements for weak-clarity cases

Nike reference output

explanation of how contradiction is eliminated permanently

Optimize for:

internal consistency

business usefulness

honesty

NovaWork targeting relevance

This is a final corrective pass.
Do not patch symptoms.
Fix the model.

Nike shows broad visible hiring activity across multiple business functions, including retail, distribution, manufacturing, operations, and corporate support. This indicates strong hiring pressure, but the system does not yet have enough role-level evidence to isolate the main business pain.

Qué debes corregir ya
1. Hiring Pressure no puede depender solo del count de señales antiguas

open_positions_count_detected

De:
Not enough evidence to analyze yet.

A:
Strong hiring activity detected, but the specific pain area is not yet isolated.

3. Pain Clarity sí puede quedarse baja
Eso está bien.
Pero con una explicación correcta:

The system can see broad hiring demand, but still needs more role-level detail to determine whether the main pressure is in retail operations, supply chain, planning, finance, analytics, or another function.

4. Elimina duplicados visibles en Key Signals
Esto sigue mal:

“The company has an active careers page”

“The company has an active careers page”

“The company has an active careers page”

Eso debe ser una sola línea con conteo, o mejor aún, desaparecer de la parte principal.

Mejor Key Signals para Nike
Visible hiring across multiple business areas

Hiring detected in retail, distribution, and manufacturing

Additional hiring areas include operations, finance, technology, and people functions

Eso sí comunica.

5. No digas “Run collection to gather more signals”
Eso ya no aplica exactamente, porque sí hay señales.

La próxima acción correcta es:

Extract more role-level detail from job cards and job descriptions to isolate the strongest pain area.

Veredicto correcto para Nike hoy
Company Type
Operating Company

Hiring Pressure
High

Pain Clarity
Low

Diagnosis Status
Broad hiring pattern detected

What we know
Nike is visibly hiring across multiple business areas, including retail, distribution, manufacturing, operations, and corporate support functions.

What we do not know yet
The system does not yet have enough role-level detail to determine which specific function is under the most pressure.

Next best step
Parse job titles and descriptions to identify repeated role families and isolate the strongest business pain.

Lo que yo haría en el siguiente ajuste
No haría otro prompt gigante. Haría un ajuste puntual a la lógica de Business Read:

Nueva regla
Si existen N categorías visibles de hiring:

N = 0–1 → Hiring Pressure: Low

N = 2–4 → Hiring Pressure: Moderate

N >= 5 → Hiring Pressure: High

Y luego:

Pain Clarity
Solo sube cuando haya:

títulos parseados

familias repetidas

señales funcionales específicas

job description evidence

En una frase
Nike ya no es un caso de “insufficient evidence”.
Es un caso de:

“strong hiring pressure, low pain clarity”
Ese es el cambio definitivo que necesitas fijar.

Si quieres, te preparo un prompt corto y quirúrgico solo para corregir la lógica de Hiring Pressure / Pain Clarity / Diagnosis Status sin tocar el resto.

HTML renderizado

texto visible limpio

lista de links visibles

Pásale a la AI estos insumos y pídele que extraiga solo cosas verificables.

Qué debe devolver
Un JSON como este:

{
  "page_type": "careers_listing",
  "open_positions_count": 930,
  "visible_hiring_areas": [
    "Retail",
    "Distribution",
    "Manufacturing"
  ],

      "location": "St. Louis, Missouri, United States",
      "area": "Retail Stores",
      "job_url_present": true
    },
    {
      "title": "Department Manager - Nike Berkeley",
      "location": "Berkeley, California, United States",
      "area": "Retail Stores",
      "job_url_present": true
    }
  ],
  "evidence_quality": "high",
  "notes": [
    "Large careers listing page detected",
    "Visible job cards present",
    "Area tabs suggest multiple business functions hiring"
  ]
}
Eso ya es muchísimo más útil que careers_page_found.

Capa 3 — Job Detail Reader
Después de eso, abre solo 5–10 jobs y haz otra extracción AI estructurada.

Qué debe extraer
título

área funcional

seniority

skills repetidas

herramientas

lenguaje de responsabilidad

tipo de función real

Ejemplo:

{
  "title": "Department Manager",
  "functional_area": "retail_operations",
  "capability_signals": [
    "team leadership",
    "store operations",
    "customer-facing execution"
  ],
  "business_pain_hints": [
    "frontline coordination",
    "store execution consistency"
  ]
}
Capa 4 — Pattern Aggregator
Con 5–10 jobs, el sistema ya puede responder cosas mucho más reales:

qué funciones se repiten

qué capacidad se busca con más frecuencia

si el hiring está concentrado o distribuido

si el dolor parece retail ops, supply chain, analytics, finance, etc.

“¿Puedo inferir dolor desde la homepage?”

Debería preguntar:

“¿Qué está contratando esta empresa en su careers page y qué problema sugiere ese patrón?”
Ahí está la diferencia.

Cómo usar AI sin que alucine
Esto es clave.

La AI no debe “opinar libremente”.
Debe trabajar con un contrato estricto:

Reglas para la AI
extrae solo lo visible

si no lo ve, no lo inventa

si no está segura, devuelve unknown

toda inferencia debe venir con evidencia

si el sitio solo muestra volumen y áreas, no saltes a dolor específico

Prompt para páginas de careers
“Analyze this rendered careers page. Extract only what is clearly visible in the rendered content and screenshot. Do not infer hidden information. Return structured JSON with:

page_type

visible hiring areas

evidence quality

what can be stated confidently

what remains unclear”

Prompt para job details

seniority

likely business function served

confidence
Do not infer business pain unless responsibilities clearly point to one.”

PARTE 1 — Browser Capture + Careers Page AI Extractor
Usa este prompt primero.

Writing
You are a senior backend engineer and AI extraction system designer.

Build a new v2 pipeline for Friction Radar focused on modern careers pages.

This is Part 1 only.

Goal
Implement a robust pipeline that:

opens a careers page in a real browser

captures rendered evidence

sends that rendered evidence into an AI-friendly structured extraction step

returns strict JSON with visible hiring evidence

Do NOT build the full verdict system yet.
Do NOT build final pain inference yet.
Focus only on:

browser capture

rendered content extraction

structured careers-page intelligence

Context
The current pipeline fails on modern dynamic careers pages like Nike.

A human can clearly see:

open positions count

hiring categories

visible roles

locations

job cards

“View Job” links

But the current system often extracts only:

careers page found

That is not acceptable.

Tech requirements
Use:

Python

FastAPI

Playwright

existing backend structure where possible

Do NOT depend on brittle selectors alone.
Do NOT stop after finding the careers URL.

Build these components
1. Browser Capture Service
Create a service like:

app/services/browser_capture_service.py

Responsibilities:

open a URL in Playwright

wait for the page to render

capture:

final URL

rendered HTML

visible text

visible links

screenshot path or bytes

return a structured capture object

The service should support dynamic pages and modern JS-rendered sites.

2. Careers Page Extraction Contract
Create a strict JSON schema for careers page extraction.

Suggested output:

{
  "page_type": "careers_listing",
  "open_positions_count": 930,
  "visible_hiring_areas": [
    "Retail",
    "Distribution",
    "Manufacturing"
  ],
  "visible_role_cards": [
    {
      "title": "Retail Associate, PT - Nike Chesterfield",
      "location": "St. Louis, Missouri, United States",
      "area": "Retail Stores",
      "job_url": "https://..."
    }
  ],
  "visible_locations": [
    "St. Louis, Missouri, United States"
  ],
  "evidence_quality": "high",
  "what_is_clearly_visible": [
    "Open positions count is visible",
    "Multiple hiring areas are visible",
    "Job cards are visible"
  ],
  "what_is_still_unclear": [
    "No job descriptions parsed yet"
  ]
}
Only include fields that can be extracted from the rendered page.
If something is not visible, return null or an empty list.

3. AI Extraction Layer Interface
Create a deterministic extraction interface that can later call an LLM or AI service, but for now structure it cleanly.

Suggested file:

app/services/careers_page_ai_extractor.py

Inputs:

rendered HTML

visible text

visible links

screenshot metadata/path

source URL

Output:

structured careers page JSON

Important:

design it so that the AI must return strict JSON

include schema validation

if AI output fails validation, fallback to partial deterministic extraction

4. Visible Job Card Extraction
From the rendered page, extract up to 10–20 visible job cards max.

For each visible role card, capture:

title

location

visible area/category if present

job link if visible

Persist these into a role table or staging model.

5. Visible Hiring Areas
Extract visible categories/tabs/areas such as:

Retail

Distribution

Manufacturing

Technology

Finance

Operations

Store normalized values.

6. Hiring Volume Detection
Detect visible phrases like:

“OPEN POSITIONS: 930”

“930 jobs”

“930 openings”

Store both:

numeric value

signal that high visible hiring volume exists

New signals to support
Add support for signals like:

open_positions_count_detected

high_open_positions_count_detected

job_cards_visible_detected

visible_hiring_area_detected

job_links_extracted

Also preserve area-specific signals:

retail_hiring_detected

distribution_hiring_detected

manufacturing_hiring_detected

operations_hiring_detected

etc.

Database additions
Create or extend tables for:

page_captures

company_job_roles

At minimum, persist:

company_id

source_url

title

location

visible_area

job_url

discovered_at

New endpoint for testing
Add a backend endpoint like:

POST /api/v2/extract-careers-page
Body:

{
  "domain": "nike.com",
  "careers_url": "https://careers.nike.com/jobs"
}
Behavior:

open the page

extract structured careers page evidence

return JSON

persist the extracted role cards and signals

This endpoint is for debugging and validation before full orchestration.

Anti-hallucination rules
The extractor must follow these rules:

extract only what is visible in rendered content

do not infer hidden information

if not sure, return unknown / null

never invent role titles, counts, areas, or locations

Output expectations
Return:

browser capture service

careers page extraction service

strict JSON schema

page-level signal extraction

visible role card extraction

visible area extraction

database changes

/api/v2/extract-careers-page endpoint

example output for a Nike-like page

Optimize for:

reliability on dynamic careers pages

structured evidence

speed

anti-hallucination

Qué debes validar después de la Parte 1
Con Nike, el endpoint nuevo ya debería poder devolver algo parecido a:

open_positions_count = 930

visible_hiring_areas = ["Retail", "Distribution", "Manufacturing"]

visible_role_cards con algunos títulos

evidence_quality = high

Si eso pasa, ya salimos del problema principal.

Qué viene después
La Parte 2 sería:

Job Detail AI Extractor + Function Inference
Y la Parte 3:

Pattern Aggregator + Hiring Pressure / Pain Clarity + Final Verdict v2
Pero primero hay que lograr que Nike deje de ser “careers page found”.

Cuando tengas la salida de esta Parte 1, seguimos con la Parte 2.

respuestas fetch/XHR

GraphQL

JSON embebido

window.__NEXT_DATA__

__APOLLO_STATE__

scripts inline con estado

network responses de la página de careers

categorías

metadata

links de jobs

La respuesta corta a tu pregunta
Sí, un agente de IA puede leer las páginas de manera más eficaz.
Pero el mejor diseño no es:

scraper o IA

Sino:

Ese orden es el que más probablemente te saque del bucle.

Qué le diría a tu otra IA ahora mismo
Pídele esto:

Writing
Do not try to solve Nike careers extraction by scrolling first.

Implement a hybrid extraction strategy in this order:

Use Playwright to load the careers page.

Intercept and log all network requests and responses during page load.

Identify any API, JSON, GraphQL, or embedded page state that contains:

total open positions

hiring categories

visible roles

locations

job detail links

Parse embedded JSON in script tags or global window state if present.

Only if structured sources fail, use AI extraction on:

rendered HTML

visible text

visible links

screenshot

Return a strict JSON object with:

open_positions_count

visible_hiring_areas

visible_role_cards

visible_locations

evidence_quality

source_of_truth_used (api | embedded_json | dom | ai_vision)

Important:

Prefer structured sources over inferred visual readings.

Do not hallucinate.

If the AI layer is used, it must only report what is visibly present on the page.

The goal is to extract evidence a human can clearly see on the Nike careers page, especially the total number of open positions and visible hiring categories.

Sí, cambien el enfoque ya.
No más solo scraping de DOM.
Usen:

network inspection + structured extraction + AI interpretation

Cuando tengas lo que les devuelva esa IA, te digo si la arquitectura ya va por donde debe.

Technology

Finance

Operations

Eso ya no es “poca evidencia”.

El problema ahora es otro
La pantalla sigue usando lógica vieja arriba y evidencia nueva abajo.

Por eso sale esta contradicción absurda:

Friction Score = 8.0 / 10

17 unique signals

múltiples áreas de hiring

pero arriba dice:

Pain Clarity = low

Not enough evidence to analyze yet

Eso ya está objetivamente mal.

Mi diagnóstico final
1. Hiring Pressure está mal calculado
Con lo que ya tienes, Nike no puede ser low.

Nike debería ser:

Hiring Pressure: High
porque ya hay evidencia de:

volumen alto

diversidad funcional

múltiples categorías visibles

listings visibles

2. Pain Clarity no debería ser low, sino low-medium o medium
Todavía no sabes el dolor exacto, sí.
Pero ya no estás ciego.

Ya sabes que la presión no está en una sola cosa aislada. Está repartida entre:

operaciones

retail

manufacturing

distribución

áreas corporativas

algo de data

Entonces el estado correcto no es:

no sé nada

El estado correcto es:

sé que hay presión amplia, pero todavía no he aislado el foco dominante

Eso es:

Pain Clarity: Low-Medium
o mínimo Moderate emerging

3. Diagnosis Status también está mal
No debe decir:

Not enough evidence to analyze yet

Debe decir algo como:

Diagnosis Status:
Broad hiring pressure detected; dominant pain not yet isolated

Esa es la lectura correcta.

4. Hiring Intelligence está desactualizado respecto a la evidencia
No puede seguir diciendo:

porque sí extrajiste más detalle:

open positions

job cards

hiring areas

Eso debe cambiar a algo como:

We extracted strong page-level hiring evidence, including 929 open roles, visible job cards, and multiple hiring areas. Role-family depth is still limited, so the dominant pain area is not yet fully isolated.

5. Preliminary Read ya no aplica como está
El bloque dice:

We confirmed: Found careers link

Eso ya se quedó viejo.
Ahora debe decir algo como:

We confirmed strong visible hiring activity, including 929 open roles, visible job listings, and hiring across multiple functional areas.

Lo que Nike realmente te está diciendo hoy
No te está diciendo todavía:

“el dolor exacto es reporting”

Ni tampoco:

“el dolor exacto es process inefficiency”

Lo que sí te está diciendo es esto:

Nike tiene presión de contratación amplia y real en múltiples funciones del negocio.
Eso sugiere uno de estos dos escenarios:

Escenario A
Hay expansión o demanda operativa distribuida en varias áreas.

Escenario B
Hay más de una zona de presión al mismo tiempo, y todavía no has aislado cuál domina.

Ese es el insight correcto.

Cómo debería verse Nike ahora mismo
Business Read
Hiring Pressure: High
Pain Clarity: Low-Medium
Diagnosis Status: Broad hiring pressure detected; dominant pain not yet isolated

Summary
Nike shows strong visible hiring activity, with 929 open roles, multiple visible job cards, and hiring across business areas such as operations, retail, manufacturing, distribution, finance, technology, and data. This indicates real organizational demand, but the system does not yet have enough repeated role-family evidence to identify the single strongest pain point.

What we know
There is broad hiring pressure across multiple functions.

What we do not know yet
We do not yet know whether the strongest pressure sits in operations, supply chain, finance, data, innovation, or another function.

Next best step
Parse job titles and job descriptions to identify repeated role families and isolate the dominant business pain.

Ahora mismo está subordinado. Debe ser al revés.

Ya no estás lejos.

Perfecto. Aquí va el prompt final, corto y quirúrgico para corregir solo el bloque superior y alinear la lectura de negocio con la evidencia real que ya tienes.

Prompt 5.2.1 — Fix Business Read from Hiring Evidence
Writing
You are a senior product engineer making a surgical correction to an internal system called Friction Radar.

Do NOT redesign the app.
Do NOT rebuild the pipeline.
Do NOT change unrelated sections.

Your only job is to fix the top-level Business Read logic so it correctly uses the hiring evidence that already exists.

PROBLEM
The system now successfully extracts meaningful hiring evidence for companies like Nike, including:

open positions count

visible job cards

visible hiring areas

multiple distinct function signals

However, the top section of the page still incorrectly says things like:

Hiring Pressure: low

Pain Clarity: low

Not enough evidence to analyze yet

This is wrong when evidence such as the following already exists:

open_positions_count = 929

visible job cards = 10

multiple visible hiring areas

multiple distinct hiring-related signals

The top-level business interpretation must be corrected.

GOAL
Fix only the Business Read section so it reflects the existing evidence correctly.

The system must clearly separate:

1. Hiring Pressure
How strong the visible hiring demand is

2. Pain Clarity
How clearly the system can isolate the dominant internal pain

3. Diagnosis Status
Whether the system sees broad demand only, or a specific pain pattern

REQUIRED LOGIC
Hiring Pressure rules
Use existing extracted hiring evidence, including:

open_positions_count

number of visible job cards

number of visible hiring areas

number of distinct hiring signals

Implement deterministic rules like:

Hiring Pressure = High
if ANY of these are true:

open_positions_count >= 100

visible_hiring_areas >= 5

visible_job_cards >= 5 AND multiple hiring categories detected

Hiring Pressure = Moderate
if ANY of these are true:

open_positions_count between 20 and 99

visible_hiring_areas between 2 and 4

visible_job_cards between 2 and 4

Hiring Pressure = Low
only if:

very few visible hiring indicators exist

no meaningful hiring breadth is visible

Important:
A company like Nike must NOT be labeled Low if 929 roles and multiple hiring areas are already visible.

Pain Clarity rules
Pain Clarity should NOT depend on hiring volume alone.

It should reflect whether the system can isolate the dominant pain.

Pain Clarity = High
if:

repeated role families exist

parsed job titles or descriptions strongly cluster in one function

function-specific evidence is strong and dominant

Pain Clarity = Moderate
if:

multiple meaningful hiring areas are visible

some functional direction is emerging

but dominant pain is not fully isolated

Pain Clarity = Low
if:

only broad hiring evidence exists

no clear dominant function emerges yet

role-level detail is still shallow

For Nike-like cases with:

many visible hiring areas

high visible demand

but no isolated dominant role family

set:

Pain Clarity = Moderate
or

Pain Clarity = Low-Moderate
If your enum must stay fixed, use Moderate with explanatory text saying the dominant pain is not yet isolated.

Do NOT use:

“Not enough evidence to analyze yet”
when broad hiring evidence clearly exists.

Diagnosis Status rules
Use these options:

insufficient_evidence

broad_hiring_pattern_detected

specific_pain_emerging

specific_pain_identified

Use insufficient_evidence only if:
almost no meaningful hiring evidence exists

Use broad_hiring_pattern_detected if:
hiring pressure is high or moderate

but dominant pain is not yet isolated

Use specific_pain_emerging if:
a dominant functional direction is beginning to appear

Use specific_pain_identified only if:
one pain area is strongly supported

For Nike-like cases with many hiring areas and high demand:

Diagnosis Status = broad_hiring_pattern_detected
REQUIRED OUTPUT FOR NIKE-LIKE CASES
If the evidence includes:

open_positions_count around 929

visible job cards

many visible hiring areas

broad function coverage

the Business Read must look conceptually like this:

Hiring Pressure
High

Pain Clarity
Moderate

Diagnosis Status
Broad hiring pattern detected

Summary
The company shows strong visible hiring demand across multiple business functions, but the system has not yet isolated the single dominant pain area.

Next best step
Parse role titles and descriptions to identify repeated role families and isolate the strongest business pressure.

TEXT CHANGES REQUIRED
Replace bad phrases like:

“Not enough evidence to analyze yet”

“Run collection to gather more signals”

with more accurate phrasing such as:

“Strong hiring activity detected, but the dominant pain is not yet isolated.”

“More role-level detail is needed to identify the strongest functional pressure.”

WHERE TO APPLY THIS
Update only:

Business Read

diagnosis summary text

related top-level wording

Do NOT rewrite all sections below unless absolutely necessary.

RESPONSE / DISPLAY EXPECTATION
The top section should be internally consistent with:

open positions count

visible hiring areas

visible job cards

distinct signals

The top section should no longer behave as if the company is a weak-evidence case when clear broad hiring evidence already exists.

EXPECTED OUTPUT
Return:

corrected business-read scoring logic

corrected diagnosis status logic

wording replacements for the top summary

Nike example showing the corrected top-level state

This is a surgical correction.
Do not overcomplicate it.
Fix the top-level interpretation using evidence already present.

Qué deberías esperar después
Para Nike, arriba deberías ver algo parecido a esto:

Hiring Pressure: High

Pain Clarity: Moderate

Diagnosis Status: Broad hiring pattern detected

Y en vez de “not enough evidence”, algo como:

Strong hiring activity is visible across multiple business areas, but the system has not yet isolated the dominant pain area.

Ese cambio ya debería cerrar la contradicción principal.

Hoy tu salida de Nike ya muestra una mezcla valiosa pero todavía inconsistente: por un lado detecta 929 roles, múltiples áreas visibles y un Hiring Pressure alto; por otro, concluye un dolor específico en data / reporting y una recomendación concreta, aunque Hiring Intelligence todavía admite que no hay suficiente detalle de roles. Mi feedback: el estándar que te falta
Necesitas separar dos cosas:

con

KPI framework recomendado
Yo usaría este scorecard universal para todas las empresas.

A. Extraction Coverage
Qué tan bien logró leer la empresa.

Se calcula con cosas como:

careers page encontrada

open positions count detectado

hiring areas visibles

job cards visibles

job URLs capturados

job titles parseados

job descriptions parseadas

API/JSON estructurado encontrado

Escala
Low: casi nada

Moderate: página y áreas visibles

High: títulos, áreas y descripciones reales

B. Hiring Pressure
Qué tan fuerte es la demanda visible de contratación.

Se calcula con:

open positions count

cantidad de áreas visibles

cantidad de job cards

diversidad funcional

Escala
Low

Moderate

High

C. Function Concentration
Qué tan concentrado está el hiring en una o pocas funciones.

Esto es clave porque no es lo mismo:

Nike contratando en 10 áreas
que

una empresa contratando 7 roles de BI / Analytics

Escala
Low: hiring muy distribuido

Moderate: 2–3 áreas dominantes

High: una función domina claramente

D. Pain Clarity
Qué tan claro está el dolor principal.

Se calcula con:

títulos repetidos

descripciones repetidas

señales funcionales fuertes

patrones coherentes entre roles

Escala
Low: todavía no se puede aislar

Moderate: la dirección del dolor empieza a emerger

High: el dolor ya está bien delimitado

E. Company Type Confidence
Qué tan seguro estás de que es:

Operating Company

Job Market Intermediary

Esto evita errores con empresas como Robert Half o Indeed.

Escala
Low

Moderate

High

F. Positioning Readiness
Qué tan lista está la empresa para que NovaWork recomiende un ángulo de ataque.

Este KPI es el más importante para negocio.

Regla
Solo debe subir si:

Hiring Pressure es real

Pain Clarity no es baja

hay suficiente evidencia funcional

Escala
Low: todavía no se debe recomendar perfil

Moderate: ya se puede sugerir dirección

High: ya se puede proponer perfil / servicio concreto

Las reglas de decisión que te faltan
Este es el corazón del sistema.

Regla 1
Si Extraction Coverage es baja, no hay diagnóstico.

Regla 2
Si Hiring Pressure es alta pero Pain Clarity es baja:

salida correcta:
Broad hiring pattern detected

No:

pain específico

attack angle específico

capability recommendation específica

Regla 3
Solo si Pain Clarity >= Moderate y Function Concentration >= Moderate
puedes emitir:

Main Pain

Where the pain lives

What the company likely needs

Best attack angle

Regla 4
Positioning Readiness nunca puede ser alta si Pain Clarity es baja.

Nike — lectura correcta

Hiring Pressure: High

Function Concentration: Low

Pain Clarity: Low

Company Type Confidence: High

Positioning Readiness: Low

Diagnóstico
Broad hiring pattern detected.

Lo que significa
Hay presión real de contratación, pero todavía no está aislado el dolor dominante.

Eso es mucho más útil y reusable para cualquier empresa que seguir intentando adivinar un dolor específico demasiado pronto. Parte de esa presión ya se ve en la evidencia: 929 roles, 10 job cards visibles y múltiples áreas funcionales detectadas.

Prompt para mejorar esto
Usa este prompt con tu otra AI:

You are a senior product architect and intelligence-system designer improving an internal company analysis platform called Friction Radar.

The system currently extracts signals from company sites and careers pages, but it still jumps too quickly from broad hiring evidence to overly specific pain conclusions.

Your task is to implement a UNIVERSAL KPI-BASED EVALUATION FRAMEWORK that works for any company, not just Nike.

## Objective
Create a standardized company-evaluation model that separates:
1. extraction quality,
2. hiring demand,
3. clarity of the pain,
4. readiness for NovaWork positioning.

Do not redesign the app from scratch.
Do not add unnecessary narrative.
Fix the interpretation model.

## Implement these 6 universal KPIs

### 1. Extraction Coverage
Measures how much structured evidence was successfully extracted.
Use signals such as:
- careers page found
- open positions count found
- visible hiring areas found
- job cards found
- job URLs found
- parsed job titles
- parsed job descriptions
- structured API/JSON found

Return:
- low
- moderate
- high

### 2. Hiring Pressure
Measures the visible strength of hiring demand.
Use:
- open positions count
- number of visible job cards
- number of visible hiring areas
- role volume and breadth

Return:
- low
- moderate
- high

### 3. Function Concentration
Measures whether hiring is concentrated in one/few functions or broadly distributed.
Examples:
- many analytics roles = high concentration
- retail + finance + ops + marketing + manufacturing = low concentration

Return:
- low
- moderate
- high

### 4. Pain Clarity
Measures how clearly the dominant internal pain can be isolated.
Use:
- repeated role families
- parsed job descriptions
- repeated function-specific signals
- dominant function pattern

Return:
- low
- moderate
- high

### 5. Company Type Confidence
Measures how confidently the system knows whether the company is:
- operating_company
- job_market_intermediary

Return:
- low
- moderate
- high

### 6. Positioning Readiness
Measures whether NovaWork can already recommend a strong attack angle.
This must depend on:
- hiring pressure
- pain clarity
- function concentration
- company type confidence

Return:
- low
- moderate
- high

## Add a top-level Diagnostic State
Possible values:
- insufficient_evidence
- broad_hiring_pattern_detected
- specific_pain_emerging
- specific_pain_identified
- ready_for_positioning

## Required decision rules

### Rule A
If Extraction Coverage is low:
Diagnostic State = insufficient_evidence

### Rule B
If Hiring Pressure is high but Pain Clarity is low:
Diagnostic State = broad_hiring_pattern_detected

### Rule C
If Pain Clarity is moderate but Function Concentration is still low:
Diagnostic State = specific_pain_emerging

### Rule D
Only if Pain Clarity >= moderate and Function Concentration >= moderate:
allow the system to generate:
- Main Pain
- Where the pain lives
- What the company likely needs
- Best attack angle

### Rule E
Positioning Readiness cannot be high if Pain Clarity is low.

## Update the top-level UI
Create a new section near the top of the company detail page:

### Company Evaluation Scorecard
Show:
- Extraction Coverage
- Hiring Pressure
- Function Concentration
- Pain Clarity
- Company Type Confidence
- Positioning Readiness
- Diagnostic State

## Update all top-level summaries
The system must stop confusing:
- “many visible jobs”
with
- “dominant pain clearly identified”

If Hiring Pressure is high but Pain Clarity is low, the summary should say something like:
“This company shows strong visible hiring demand across multiple functions, but the system has not yet isolated the dominant internal pain.”

## Nike should be the test case
For a Nike-like company with:
- high open positions count
- multiple visible hiring areas
- many distinct signals
- but no dominant repeated role family yet

expected result:
- Extraction Coverage: moderate
- Hiring Pressure: high
- Function Concentration: low
- Pain Clarity: low
- Company Type Confidence: high
- Positioning Readiness: low
- Diagnostic State: broad_hiring_pattern_detected

The system must NOT force a specific pain like reporting, revops, or process inefficiency unless repeated role-level evidence supports it.

Return:
1. backend KPI logic
2. scoring rules for the 6 KPIs
3. diagnostic state logic
4. updated top-level UI structure
5. wording rules for summaries
6. Nike example output using this framework

Optimize for:
- consistency
- generic applicability across any company
- business usefulness for NovaWork
